# Changelog

All notable changes to this project will be documented in this file.

The format is inspired by Keep a Changelog, adapted for Foundry's pre-`1.0` releases.

## [Unreleased]

### Security

- TOTP MFA now uses HMAC-SHA1 per RFC 6238 so codes verify against mainstream authenticator apps (Google Authenticator, Authy, 1Password, etc.), which ignore the otpauth `algorithm` parameter and always compute SHA1. **TOTP factors enrolled on previous builds generate different codes and must be re-enrolled.**
- `min_numeric`, `max_numeric`, and `between` validation rules now reject values that fail to parse as a number, as well as `NaN` and infinities; previously non-numeric input (including `"NaN"`, which defeats all numeric comparisons) silently passed bound checks. The `numeric` rule is now parse-based: malformed shapes like `"1.2.3"` are rejected, and scientific notation such as `"1e10"` is accepted.
- The Postgres compiler now validates `EXTRACT` field names against the known date/time fields and restricts `Sql::op` custom operators to legal operator characters, closing a raw-SQL interpolation path if either was ever fed untrusted input.
- Password-reset and email-verification tokens now enforce their TTL inside the consuming `DELETE`, so presenting an expired token no longer destroys it; expired and unknown tokens return the same "invalid or expired" message.
- `StaticBearerAuthenticator` stores and compares SHA-256 digests of its tokens instead of plaintext map keys, removing token-comparison timing as a side channel.
- Secret-bearing config structs (`AppConfig.signing_key`, SMTP/Resend/Postmark/Mailgun/SES credentials, S3 secret) redact their secrets in `Debug` output, and `DatabaseConfig`/`RedisConfig` redact URL credentials, so `{:?}` logging can no longer leak credentials.

### Added

- `TsValidationSchema::deny_unknown_fields_with_known_fields(...)` now provides a one-call manual-schema builder for strict frontend unknown-field validation with the full backend-owned public field list. This reduces the chance that hand-written schemas call `.deny_unknown_fields()` but forget fields that have no direct validation rules. **Consumer follow-up:** no breaking change; manual schemas may replace `.deny_unknown_fields().known_fields([...])` with the new helper.
- AppEnum alias metadata is now part of the backend-owned enum SSOT. `EnumOption` includes `aliases`, generated TypeScript option rows include those aliases, `FoundryAppEnum::accepted_keys()` exposes canonical keys plus aliases, `.app_enum::<E>()` validation accepts the same values, each AppEnum file exports `{Enum}Aliases`, `{Enum}Alias`, alias selectors/guards, and `get{Enum}CanonicalValue(...)`, and `parse{Enum}OrNull(...)` now mirrors `FoundryAppEnum::parse_key(...)` by accepting declared aliases and returning the canonical enum value. Duplicate aliases, blank aliases, and alias/canonical-value collisions fail fast during derive or manual TypeScript metadata export. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime. Rust code that manually constructs `EnumOption` must add `aliases: Vec::new()` or the intended alias list; frontend code that used `parse{Enum}OrNull(...)` as a canonical-only check should use `is{Enum}(...)` instead.
- Storage now includes a built-in in-memory disk driver (`driver = "memory"`) for tests, local fakes, and ephemeral workflows. It supports the standard storage operations, participates in generated storage manifests as a configured `memory` driver disk, and intentionally does not support public or temporary URL generation. **Consumer follow-up:** no breaking change unless an app registered a custom storage driver named `memory`; rename that custom driver or switch to the built-in disk before upgrading.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint runtime now exposes request-metadata presence helpers on endpoint instances and state snapshots: `endpoint.hasRequestSchema()`, `endpoint.hasRequestTransport()`, `endpoint.hasRequestMediaType()`, `endpoint.hasRequestMetadata()`, plus `FoundryEndpointState.hasRequestSchema`, `hasRequestTransport`, `hasRequestMediaType`, and `hasRequestMetadata`. Endpoint-aware forms, docs panels, and custom clients can branch on backend-owned request schema/transport/media metadata without duplicating `!== null` checks. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime. Apps that manually construct `FoundryEndpointState` objects must add the four boolean fields or derive snapshots from `endpoint.state()`.
- Generated TypeScript route helpers now export static request-metadata presence constants: `{RouteName}HasRequestSchema`, `{RouteName}HasRequestTransport`, `{RouteName}HasRequestMediaType`, and `{RouteName}HasRequestMetadata`. Route docs, schema explorers, custom transports, and generated-client dashboards can branch on route-local backend-owned request metadata without local `{RouteName}RequestSchema !== null` wrappers. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime; replace local static route-helper request metadata predicates with the generated constants where request metadata is backend-owned.
- Generated TypeScript `prepareSubmit(...)` envelopes now include static route/request metadata: `routeName`, `path`, `requestSchema`, `requestTransport`, `requestMediaType`, `hasRequestSchema`, `hasRequestTransport`, `hasRequestMediaType`, and `hasRequestMetadata`. Custom transports, debug panels, request previews, and generated-client dashboards can pass a self-contained prepared request object without separately carrying endpoint route metadata. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime. Code that manually constructs `FoundryPreparedSubmitRequest` objects must add the new metadata fields or derive envelopes from `endpoint.prepareSubmit(...)`.
- Rust `RouteRegistry::url` and generated TypeScript route URL/match helpers now parse route templates segment-by-segment from the same backend route rules: `{id}`, `{*path}`, and segment-leading legacy `:id` remain params, while literal colon text inside a segment such as `v1:beta` is no longer substituted or matched as a fake param. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime; strict `RouteManifest.ts` snapshots should allow the URL/matcher runtime change, and any code that relied on literal colon text as a param should define an explicit backend route param segment instead.
- Signed route URL generation now rejects extra query parameters named `expires` or `signature` before signing, instead of producing a URL that `verify_signed_url(...)` immediately rejects as duplicated/tampered. Path parameters with those names are still allowed when they are consumed by the route path. **Consumer follow-up:** rename signed-route extra query parameters that use `expires` or `signature`, or move domain data into differently named keys before calling `signed_route_url(...)`.
- Rust `RouteRegistry::url` / `AppContext::route_url` now reject duplicate path parameter keys instead of silently letting one slice entry replace another during URL construction, matching generated TypeScript's object-shaped path params. Repeated non-path query keys are still preserved as repeated query params. **Consumer follow-up:** remove duplicate path-param entries such as repeated `("id", ...)` pairs before calling `route_url(...)`; keep repeated query filters on non-path keys if that shape is intentional.
- Route path validation now rejects malformed empty parameter tokens such as `{}`, `{*}`, and `:` across Rust URL generation, OpenAPI generation, and direct TypeScript `RouteManifest` export instead of silently treating them as literals or omitting required params. **Consumer follow-up:** replace empty route parameter tokens with named segments such as `{id}`, `{*path}`, or `:id` before regenerating OpenAPI/frontend types.
- Generated OpenAPI operations for typed body requests now include `x-foundry-request-media-type` (`"application/json"` / `"multipart/form-data"`) from the same backend-owned decision used by `RouteManifest.requestMediaType` and generated TypeScript submit defaults. Query-transport typed requests omit the extension, matching `requestMediaType: null`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate OpenAPI clients/docs; strict OpenAPI snapshots should allow the additive extension, and custom tooling can read it instead of inspecting `requestBody.content` keys.
- Generated OpenAPI response objects now include `x-foundry-response-has-body` for every documented response and `x-foundry-response-media-type` (`"application/json"` / `"application/octet-stream"`) for body-bearing responses, using the same backend-owned no-content, `Unit`, and file-response rules as `RouteManifestResponse.hasBody` / `mediaType`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate OpenAPI clients/docs; strict OpenAPI snapshots should allow the additive extensions, and custom tooling can read them instead of inferring response body/media metadata from `responses[*].content`.
- App-backed OpenAPI specs now publish registered custom validation rules in a top-level `x-foundry-validation-rules` map using the same `{ id, serverOnly: true }` metadata as generated `ValidationRuleManifest.ts`; standalone OpenAPI generation remains non-authoritative and omits the manifest. OpenAPI generation now also rejects validation rule ids that duplicate, contain empty dotted segments, mix parent ids with child id groups, or collide after generated `ValidationRuleIds` camelCase normalization. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate OpenAPI clients/docs; strict OpenAPI snapshots should allow the additive extension, OpenAPI-driven form/docs tooling can read it instead of duplicating the custom validation rule registry, and any duplicate or normalized-colliding custom rule ids should be renamed or deduplicated.
- Generated OpenAPI `x-foundry-auth` metadata now includes `allowsMfaPendingToken` and `hasAuthorizeCallback` beside the existing `required`, `guard`, and `permissions` fields, using the same backend-owned route options as `RouteManifest.allowsMfaPendingToken` / `hasAuthorizeCallback`. OpenAPI-driven docs, route audits, and generated clients can distinguish MFA verification routes and dynamic-authorizer routes without duplicating Foundry route setup, and OpenAPI generation now rejects malformed direct auth metadata before writing `x-foundry-auth`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate OpenAPI clients/docs; strict OpenAPI snapshots should allow the additive fields, direct route-doc auth metadata should use trimmed unique guard/permission rows, and guard/permission/authorize-callback metadata should only appear when auth is required.
- Generated OpenAPI operations for named routes now include `x-foundry-route-id`, preserving the canonical backend route id even when `operationId` is overridden for client method names. OpenAPI generation now also rejects emitted route ids that duplicate, contain empty dotted segments, mix parent route ids with child route-id groups, or collide after generated `RouteIds` camelCase normalization, matching the generated route manifest's route-id SSOT expectations. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate OpenAPI clients/docs; strict OpenAPI snapshots should allow the additive extension, and any duplicate or normalized-colliding documented named routes should be renamed or deduplicated.
- Generated OpenAPI operations now include `x-foundry-route-policy` when routes have backend-owned policy metadata, including resolved `middlewareGroup`, resolved `auditArea`, and route-level `rateLimits` rows with `maxRequests`, `windowSeconds`, and `by`. This mirrors the generated `RouteManifest` policy surface for OpenAPI-driven docs, audits, and generated clients while keeping backend-only rate-limit key prefixes private, and OpenAPI generation now rejects malformed policy metadata before writing those rows: blank/padded middleware groups or audit areas, zero or JavaScript-unsafe route-level limiter windows, unknown limiter `by` values, and public actor-only limiter rows. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate OpenAPI clients/docs; strict OpenAPI snapshots should allow the additive extension, and route-level `RateLimit::new(...)` / direct policy metadata should use trimmed policy text plus positive browser-safe windows with `ip`, `actor`, or `actor_or_ip` keying, with `actor` only on authenticated routes.
- Generated TypeScript `RouteManifest` entries now expose inherited route middleware group metadata as `middlewareGroup`, with route-local helpers `routeMiddlewareGroup(...)`, `routeMiddlewareGroupOrNull(...)`, `routeHasMiddlewareGroup(...)`, and group selectors such as `routesWithMiddlewareGroup(...)`, `routesWithAnyMiddlewareGroup()`, `routesWithoutMiddlewareGroup()`, plus count/presence/first/route-name companions. Route audits, docs panels, generated clients, and frontend navigation can read backend-owned middleware grouping without duplicating route setup knowledge. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime. Rust code that manually constructs `RouteManifestEntry` must add `middleware_group`, and custom TypeScript `RouteManifestEntry` fixtures must add `middlewareGroup`.
- Generated TypeScript `RouteManifest` entries now expose resolved route audit metadata as `auditArea`, with route-local helpers `routeAuditArea(...)`, `routeAuditAreaOrNull(...)`, `routeHasAuditArea(...)`, and audit-area selectors such as `routesWithAuditArea(...)`, `routesWithAnyAuditArea()`, `routesWithoutAuditArea()`, plus count/presence/first/route-name companions. Audit dashboards, admin navigation, generated docs, and route policy checks can read backend-owned audit areas without duplicating scope setup knowledge. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime. Rust code that manually constructs `RouteManifestEntry` must add `audit_area`, and custom TypeScript `RouteManifestEntry` fixtures must add `auditArea`.
- Generated TypeScript `RouteManifest` entries now expose effective route-level rate-limit metadata as `rateLimits`, with route-local helpers `routeRateLimits(...)`, `routeRateLimitsOrNull(...)`, `routeRateLimitCount(...)`, `routeHasRateLimits(...)`, `routeHasRateLimitBy(...)`, `routeFirstRateLimit(...)`, and route selectors such as `routesWithRateLimits()`, `routesWithoutRateLimits()`, `routesWithRateLimitBy(...)`, plus count/presence/first/route-name companions. Route audits, admin diagnostics, API docs, and generated clients can read backend-owned route limiter policy without duplicating `RateLimit::new(...)` setup; backend-only key prefixes are not exported, and `windowSeconds` now fails export when it exceeds JavaScript's safe integer range. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime. Rust code that manually constructs `RouteManifestEntry` must add `rate_limits` with positive browser-safe `window_seconds`, and custom TypeScript `RouteManifestEntry` fixtures must add `rateLimits`.
- Generated TypeScript `RouteManifest` entries now expose MFA pending-token exceptions as `allowsMfaPendingToken`, with route-local helpers `routeAllowsMfaPendingToken(...)`, `routeAllowsMfaPendingTokenOrNull(...)`, `routeRejectsMfaPendingToken(...)`, and route selectors such as `routesAllowingMfaPendingToken()` / `routesRejectingMfaPendingToken()` plus count/presence/first/route-name companions. MFA flows, route guards, and auth diagnostics can read backend-owned verification-route exceptions without duplicating route lists. `HttpRouteBuilder` now also mirrors `HttpRouteOptions::allow_mfa_pending_token()` for scoped route closure DX. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime. Rust code that manually constructs `RouteManifestEntry` must add `allows_mfa_pending_token`, and custom TypeScript `RouteManifestEntry` fixtures must add `allowsMfaPendingToken`.
- Generated TypeScript `RouteManifest` entries now expose dynamic backend route authorization callbacks as `hasAuthorizeCallback`, with route-local helpers `routeHasAuthorizeCallback(...)` / `routeHasAuthorizeCallbackOrNull(...)` and route selectors such as `routesWithAuthorizeCallback()` / `routesWithoutAuthorizeCallback()` plus count/presence/first/route-name companions. Route guards, policy audits, and generated docs can distinguish callback-protected routes from guard/permission-only routes without duplicating route setup knowledge. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime. Rust code that manually constructs `RouteManifestEntry` must add `has_authorize_callback`, and custom TypeScript `RouteManifestEntry` fixtures must add `hasAuthorizeCallback`.
- `HttpScope` now mirrors the route option defaults for MFA pending-token allowance and endpoint helper export toggles with `allow_mfa_pending_token()`, `client_export(...)`, and `without_client_export()`. Scoped auth/MFA route trees can define those backend-owned defaults once instead of repeating them on every child route or dropping down to `group_with_options()`. **Consumer follow-up:** no breaking change; apps may replace repeated child-route calls with the new scope defaults.
- `HttpScope` now mirrors route documentation helpers for inherited request schemas, shared responses, and Foundry's standard validation error envelope with `request::<T>()`, `response::<T>(status)`, and `validation_errors()`. Generated OpenAPI, `RouteManifest`, and TypeScript endpoint helpers now receive those backend-owned docs from the same scoped route tree instead of requiring repeated child-route calls. **Consumer follow-up:** no breaking change; scope-level responses apply to every child route, so only move repeated responses into a scope when that response is intentionally shared.
- CLI command descriptors and generated `CommandManifest.ts` now distinguish flat Clap argument names from split `positionalArguments`, `argumentMetadata`, non-positional `options`, value-taking `valueOptions`, and flag-style `flags` metadata, including kind/help/long-help/required/repeatable/value-name/value-hint/default-value/possible-value hints, matching counts validated against their arrays and TypeScript's safe integer range, typed names, guards, nullable parsers, selected filters such as `commandsWithPositionalArgument(...)` / `commandsWithValueOption(...)` / `commandsWithFlag(...)`, grouped selectors such as `commandsWithPositionalArguments()` / `commandsWithValueOptions()` / `commandsWithFlags()`, argument metadata helpers such as `commandArgumentMetadata(...)`, `commandArgumentHelp(...)`, `commandArgumentPossibleValues(...)`, `commandRequiredArgumentNames(...)`, `commandRepeatableArgumentNames(...)`, and `commandDefaultedArgumentNames(...)`, and option switch metadata/helpers such as `commandOptionSwitches(...)`, `commandOptionTokens(...)`, and `commandPreferredOptionTokenOrNull(...)`. CLI dashboards, command palettes, generated admin tooling, and command-form builders can model positional inputs, text/value option controls, boolean/count flags, labels/help text, placeholders, completion hints, select choices, required fields, repeatable inputs, default values, and actual `--long` / `-s` tokens without scraping Clap output or locally filtering `CommandManifest`. **Consumer follow-up:** apps that only register commands do not need code changes; regenerate frontend types/runtime to consume the new helpers. Rust code that manually constructs `CommandDescriptor` must add `argument_metadata`, `positional_arguments`, `options`, `option_switches`, `value_options`, `flags`, and matching `*_count` fields that equal their array lengths and stay below TypeScript's safe integer limit.
- `db:migrate:status --json` summary output now includes `drifted` and `up_to_date` booleans derived from the backend migration ledger, registered migration set, and missing-applied drift report. Deploy tooling can branch on the SSOT status directly instead of duplicating count logic. **Consumer follow-up:** no migration SQL changes; strict JSON decoders for migration status summaries should allow the two additive fields.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint runtime now exports `foundryValidationRuleFieldReferencesForField(...)` plus count, first, nullable-first, presence, and predicate companions for resolving a rule's sibling-field references against a concrete nested/indexed field path. It also exports `foundryValidationSchemaFieldRuleReferencesField(...)` and a matching `FoundryEndpoint.validationSchemaFieldRuleReferencesField(...)` facade for field+rule-code dependency checks. Nested form adapters can revalidate sibling dependencies at `children[0].password_confirmation`, `[tenant].password_confirmation`, or `items[0].password_confirmation` without copying Foundry's internal path resolver. **Consumer follow-up:** no breaking change; regenerate frontend types/runtime and replace local sibling-reference path normalization or resolved-reference predicate checks with the generated helpers where validation metadata is backend-owned.
- Generated TypeScript validation schemas now include backend-owned field value kind metadata for non-scalar contract fields (`array`, `map`, `json`, `file`, and `nested`), and generated client-side cross-field rules use it when comparing sibling references. Rules such as `required_with`, `required_if`, `accepted_if`, `same`, and temporal comparisons now mirror Rust's presence/comparable value semantics for arrays, maps, JSON values, uploaded files, and nested DTOs instead of treating raw JavaScript objects as scalar strings. OpenAPI request schemas and expanded query operations also expose the same rows as `x-foundry-validation-field-value-kinds`. `TsValidationSchema::field_value_kind(...)` is available for manual schemas, and the new `TsValidationFieldValueKind` / `TsValidationFieldValueKindEntry` types are exported from the prelude. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime and OpenAPI clients/docs. Rust code that manually constructs `TsValidationSchema` with a struct literal must add `field_value_kinds: Vec::new()` or the intended entries; hand-written schemas with cross-field rules referencing non-scalar fields should call `.field_value_kind(...)` so frontend validation matches the backend. Strict generated-TS snapshots should allow optional `fieldValueKinds` arrays and the new runtime helpers; strict OpenAPI snapshots should allow the additive `x-foundry-validation-field-value-kinds` extension.
- `TsValidationRule` now mirrors the runtime validation DSL with additive manual-schema helpers for `size_numeric(...)`, `starts_with_value(...)`, `doesnt_start_with_value(...)`, `ends_with_value(...)`, `doesnt_end_with_value(...)`, `contains_value(...)`, `doesnt_contain_value(...)`, `starts_with_any(...)`, `doesnt_start_with_any(...)`, `ends_with_any(...)`, and `doesnt_end_with_any(...)`. They emit the existing canonical `size`, `starts_with`, `doesnt_start_with`, `ends_with`, `doesnt_end_with`, `contains`, and `doesnt_contain` metadata, so derived schemas and hand-written backend-owned TypeScript validation contracts stay aligned. **Consumer follow-up:** no breaking change; regenerate frontend types/runtime if a consumer wants to replace local manual metadata wrappers with these helpers.
- Generated TypeScript validation and response metadata helpers now export nullable companions for direct optional lookups, not only first selectors. New helpers include `foundryValidationSchemaContainerOrNull(...)`, `foundryValidationSchemaReachableRuleOrNull(...)`, `foundryValidationSchemaRuleParamOrNull(...)`, `foundryValidationSchemaRuleSchemaOrNull(...)`, `foundryValidationSchemaFieldRuleParamOrNull(...)`, `foundryValidationSchemaFieldRuleSchemaOrNull(...)`, `foundryValidationRuleParamOrNull(...)`, `foundryValidationRuleSchemaOrNull(...)`, `foundryValidationRuleCustomRuleIdOrNull(...)`, `{RouteName}ResponseMetadataForStatusOrNull(...)`, and `endpoint.responseMetadataForStatusOrNull(...)`; matching `FoundryEndpoint` validation-schema mirrors are generated as well. This completes the public generated TypeScript `| undefined` helper surface with explicit `null` alternatives for consumers that standardize on nullable contracts. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime; replace local direct lookup `... ?? null` wrappers for validation schema/rule metadata or route response status metadata with the generated helpers where metadata is backend-owned.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint validation schema helpers now export nullable companions for every schema/field first selector, including `foundryValidationSchemaFirstRuleOrNull(...)`, `foundryValidationSchemaFirstReachableRuleOrNull(...)`, `foundryValidationSchemaFieldFirstRuleOrNull(...)`, `foundryValidationSchemaFieldFirstRuleCodeOrNull(...)`, `foundryValidationSchemaFirstMessageOrNull(...)`, `foundryValidationSchemaFirstAttributeOrNull(...)`, `foundryValidationSchemaFirstKnownFieldOrNull(...)`, and `foundryValidationSchemaFirstUnknownFieldOrNull(...)`; `FoundryEndpoint` mirrors the same `validationSchema...OrNull(...)` methods. Form builders, validation inspectors, and generated docs can use explicit `null` contracts instead of local validation-schema first selector `... ?? null` wrappers. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime; replace local validation-schema first-value nullable wrappers with the generated helpers where endpoint validation metadata is backend-owned.
- Generated TypeScript route endpoint helpers and `FoundryEndpoint` instances now export nullable response-summary first-selector companions for documented status, schema, media-type, and body-flag lists: `{RouteName}FirstResponseStatusOrNull`, `{RouteName}FirstResponseSchemaOrNull`, `{RouteName}FirstResponseMediaTypeOrNull`, `{RouteName}FirstResponseBodyFlagOrNull`, `endpoint.firstResponseStatusOrNull()`, `endpoint.firstResponseSchemaOrNull()`, `endpoint.firstResponseMediaTypeOrNull()`, and `endpoint.firstResponseBodyFlagOrNull()`. Endpoint-aware forms, docs panels, and response adapters can use explicit `null` contracts instead of local response summary `... ?? null` wrappers. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime; replace local endpoint response-summary first-value nullable wrappers with the generated helpers where route response metadata is backend-owned.
- Generated TypeScript route endpoint helpers and `FoundryEndpoint` instances now export nullable response-metadata first-selector companions for schema, media type, and body filters: `{RouteName}FirstResponseMetadataForSchemaOrNull(...)`, `{RouteName}FirstResponseMetadataForMediaTypeOrNull(...)`, `{RouteName}FirstResponseMetadataForBodyOrNull(...)`, `endpoint.firstResponseMetadataForSchemaOrNull(...)`, `endpoint.firstResponseMetadataForMediaTypeOrNull(...)`, and `endpoint.firstResponseMetadataForBodyOrNull(...)`. Route docs, download adapters, and no-content checks can use explicit `null` contracts instead of local endpoint response metadata `... ?? null` wrappers. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime; replace local endpoint response-metadata first-value nullable wrappers with the generated helpers where route response metadata is backend-owned.
- Generated TypeScript `DatabaseManifest.ts` now exports `databaseFirstPaginationQueryParamNameOrNull()`, a nullable companion to `databaseFirstPaginationQueryParamName()`. List screens, router adapters, and generated clients can use explicit `null` contracts instead of local database pagination query-param first selector `... ?? null` wrappers. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime; replace local database pagination first-value nullable wrappers with the generated helper where pagination metadata is backend-owned.
- Generated TypeScript AppEnum files now export nullable first-selector companions for value, option, string-key, and dotted-group metadata: `get{Name}FirstValueOrNull()`, `get{Name}FirstOptionOrNull()`, `get{Name}FirstKeyNameOrNull()`, `get{Name}FirstKeyValueOrNull()`, `get{Name}FirstGroupNameOrNull()`, and `get{Name}FirstGroupOrNull()`. Enum-driven filters, selects, permission menus, and admin scaffolds can use explicit `null` contracts instead of local AppEnum first selector `... ?? null` wrappers. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime; replace local AppEnum first-value nullable wrappers with the generated helpers where enum metadata is backend-owned.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint validation runtime now exports nullable first-selector companions for validation rule-code lists and rule metadata arrays: `foundryClientValidationFirstRuleCodeOrNull()`, `foundryValidationControlFirstRuleCodeOrNull()`, `foundryValidationRequiredFirstRuleCodeOrNull()`, `foundryValidationFieldReferenceFirstRuleCodeOrNull()`, `foundryValidationRuntimeFirstRuleCodeOrNull()`, `foundryValidationRuleFirstValueOrNull(rule)`, `foundryValidationRuleFirstFieldReferenceOrNull(rule)`, and `foundryValidationRuleFirstNestedRuleOrNull(rule)`. Form builders, validation inspectors, and generated validation docs can use explicit `null` contracts instead of local validation runtime first selector `... ?? null` wrappers. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime; replace local validation runtime first-value nullable wrappers with the generated helpers where endpoint validation metadata is backend-owned.
- Generated TypeScript `DatatableManifest.ts` and `NotificationManifest.ts` now export nullable first-selector companions for backend-owned table and notification metadata lists. Datatable helpers include `datatableFirstEntryOrNull()`, `datatableFirstNameOrNull()`, column/name group companions such as `datatableFirstColumnOrNull()`, `datatableFirstSortableFieldNameOrNull()`, `datatableFirstFilterableColumnNameOrNull()`, `datatableFirstExportableColumnOrNull()`, `datatableFirstRelationColumnNameOrNull()`, relation-specific companions such as `datatableFirstColumnForRelationOrNull(...)`, `datatableFirstRelationFilterFieldNameForRelationOrNull(...)`, `datatableFirstRelationFilterForRelationOrNull(...)`, `datatableFirstRelationFilterFieldForRelationOrNull(...)`, and aggregate metadata companions such as `datatableFirstMappingNameOrNull()`, `datatableFirstRelationFilterOrNull()`, `datatableFirstStaticFilterFieldNameOrNull()`, and `datatableFirstDefaultSortOrNull()`. Notification helpers include `notificationFirstTypeOrNull()`, `notificationFirstChannelNameOrNull()`, `notificationFirstEntryOrNull()`, `notificationFirstPayloadNameOrNull()`, `notificationFirstEntryWithPayloadOrNull(payload)`, `notificationFirstEntryWithoutPayloadOrNull(payload)`, `notificationFirstTypeWithPayloadOrNull(payload)`, and `notificationFirstTypeWithoutPayloadOrNull(payload)`. Table builders, filter UIs, export dialogs, notification dashboards, and broadcast tooling can use explicit `null` contracts instead of local datatable or notification first selector `... ?? null` wrappers. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime; replace local datatable or notification first-value nullable wrappers with the generated helpers where table or notification metadata is backend-owned.
- Generated TypeScript `WebSocketChannelManifest.ts` now exports nullable first-selector companions for channel metadata lists, including `webSocketFirstChannelOrNull()`, `webSocketFirstChannelNameOrNull()`, `webSocketFirstPresenceChannelOrNull()`, `webSocketFirstPresenceChannelNameOrNull()`, `webSocketFirstNonPresenceChannelOrNull()`, `webSocketFirstNonPresenceChannelNameOrNull()`, `webSocketFirstClientEventChannelOrNull()`, `webSocketFirstClientEventChannelNameOrNull()`, `webSocketFirstChannelDisallowingClientEventsOrNull()`, `webSocketFirstChannelNameDisallowingClientEventsOrNull()`, `webSocketFirstAuthRequiredChannelOrNull()`, `webSocketFirstAuthRequiredChannelNameOrNull()`, `webSocketFirstPublicChannelOrNull()`, `webSocketFirstPublicChannelNameOrNull()`, `webSocketFirstChannelWithGuardOrNull(guard)`, `webSocketFirstChannelNameWithGuardOrNull(guard)`, `webSocketFirstChannelWithAnyGuardOrNull()`, `webSocketFirstChannelNameWithAnyGuardOrNull()`, `webSocketFirstChannelWithoutGuardOrNull()`, `webSocketFirstChannelNameWithoutGuardOrNull()`, `webSocketFirstChannelWithReplayOrNull()`, `webSocketFirstChannelNameWithReplayOrNull()`, `webSocketFirstChannelWithoutReplayOrNull()`, `webSocketFirstChannelNameWithoutReplayOrNull()`, `webSocketChannelFirstPermissionOrNull(name)`, `webSocketFirstChannelWithPermissionsOrNull()`, `webSocketFirstChannelNameWithPermissionsOrNull()`, `webSocketFirstChannelWithoutPermissionsOrNull()`, `webSocketFirstChannelNameWithoutPermissionsOrNull()`, `webSocketFirstChannelWithPermissionOrNull(permission)`, `webSocketFirstChannelNameWithPermissionOrNull(permission)`, `webSocketChannelFirstClientEventOrNull(name)`, `webSocketFirstChannelWithClientEventsOrNull()`, `webSocketFirstChannelNameWithClientEventsOrNull()`, `webSocketFirstChannelWithoutClientEventsOrNull()`, `webSocketFirstChannelNameWithoutClientEventsOrNull()`, `webSocketChannelFirstServerEventOrNull(name)`, `webSocketFirstChannelWithServerEventsOrNull()`, `webSocketFirstChannelNameWithServerEventsOrNull()`, `webSocketFirstChannelWithoutServerEventsOrNull()`, and `webSocketFirstChannelNameWithoutServerEventsOrNull()`. - Generated TypeScript endpoint `validateFieldAndDependents(...)` now maps schema-level dependent fields back onto the changed field's concrete runtime path before revalidating. Changing `[0].password`, `[tenant].password`, `items[0].password`, or `children[0].password` refreshes the matching confirmation/conditional sibling at the same address instead of clearing and revalidating every unindexed dependent across the root container or nested array. - Generated TypeScript endpoint instances now expose schema/media/body response metadata filters: `hasResponseSchema(...)`, `responseMetadataForSchema(...)`, `firstResponseMetadataForSchema(...)`, `hasResponseMediaType(...)`, `responseMetadataForMediaType(...)`, `firstResponseMetadataForMediaType(...)`, `hasResponseBody(...)`, `responseMetadataForBody(...)`, and `firstResponseMetadataForBody(...)`. Schema explorers, download adapters, no-content checks, and docs panels can branch or render cloned backend-owned response metadata rows without local `responseMetadata.some(...)`, `.filter(...)`, or `.find(...)` scans. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime; replace endpoint-local response metadata schema/media/body predicates and filters with the generated methods where response metadata is backend-owned.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint instances and `state()` snapshots now expose count, presence, and first-value helpers for backend-owned response metadata arrays: `responseStatusCount()`, `hasResponseStatuses()`, `firstResponseStatus()`, `responseSchemaCount()`, `hasResponseSchemas()`, `firstResponseSchema()`, `responseMediaTypeCount()`, `hasResponseMediaTypes()`, `firstResponseMediaType()`, `responseBodyFlagCount()`, `hasResponseBodyFlags()`, `firstResponseBodyFlag()`, and matching snapshot fields. Schema explorers, docs, status tabs, download adapters, and no-content checks can render response metadata summaries without local `.length > 0`, `.length`, or `[0]` wrappers. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime; replace endpoint-local response metadata count/presence/first wrappers with the generated methods or snapshot fields. Tests or stores that manually construct `FoundryEndpointState` must include the new response metadata summary fields or derive state from `endpoint.state()`.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint instances and `state()` snapshots now expose response schema/media/body arrays through `responseSchemas()`, `responseMediaTypes()`, `responseBodyFlags()`, and matching `FoundryEndpointState` fields. Schema explorers, download adapters, no-content checks, docs, and status-aware stores can reuse backend-owned response metadata without local `endpoint.responseMetadata.map(...)` helpers. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime; replace endpoint-local response schema/media/body map helpers with the generated methods or snapshot fields. Tests or stores that manually construct `FoundryEndpointState` must include `responseSchemas`, `responseMediaTypes`, and `responseBodyFlags` or derive state from `endpoint.state()`.
- Generated TypeScript route helpers now export `{RouteName}RequestSchema` plus `{RouteName}RequestSchemaName`, `{RouteName}RequestTransportValue`, and `{RouteName}RequestMediaTypeValue` aliases, and generated endpoint instances/state snapshots expose `requestSchema`. Schema explorers, debug panels, custom transports, and route docs can read route-local request schema/transport/media metadata without local `RouteManifest` lookups or `typeof ...` wrappers. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime; replace local route request metadata aliases with the generated exports. Custom `FoundryEndpoint` subclasses must provide `requestSchema`, and tests or stores that manually construct `FoundryEndpointState` must include `requestSchema` or derive state from `endpoint.state()`.
- Generated TypeScript successful response hydration now clones HTTP response envelopes/data before storing endpoint `response` / `rawResponse`, clones `state().response` / `state().rawResponse` snapshots, and passes a cloned envelope to `onSuccess(response)`. Endpoint success state can no longer be mutated silently by changing the HTTP client response object, a state snapshot, or the `onSuccess(...)` argument. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime; code that intentionally mutated `onSuccess(response)` or `endpoint.state().response` to update generated endpoint state should call `applyResponse(...)` with the updated response or keep derived display state outside the endpoint.
- Generated TypeScript submit preparation now clones endpoint data before passing it to `transform(data)`, clones `options.data` / transform return values before validation and request serialization, and passes a cloned payload to `onStart(data)`. `submit(...)`, `submitForm(...)`, `submitResponse(...)`, `submitUrl(...)`, `submitMode(...)`, and `prepareSubmit(...)` can no longer mutate endpoint state or the eventual request body through shared submit payload references. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime; transform callbacks that intentionally mutated their input should return the transformed payload, and `onStart(...)` callbacks that intentionally changed the outgoing request should move that logic into `transform(...)`.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint write APIs now clone accepted request/form and route-param values at ownership boundaries, including construction, `setData(...)`, `patchData(...)`, `setField(...)` / validation variants, `setParams(...)`, `patchParams(...)`, `applyValidationResult(...)`, server-error hydration, and upload progress storage. Endpoint state can no longer be mutated silently by changing an object after passing it into a generated setter, while file/blob/form-data handles remain shared. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime; code that intentionally passed mutable objects into generated setters and then mutated those same objects to update endpoint state should call generated setters again (`setData(...)`, `patchData(...)`, `setField(...)`, `setParams(...)`, etc.) so subscribers are notified.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint `state()` snapshots, endpoint `validationResult()`, and `FoundryValidationClientError` now clone request/form/response-state values (`data`, `initialData`, `routeParams`, `touched`, `errors`, `errorDetails`, `progress`, `response`, `rawResponse`, `responseMetadata`, `responseStatuses`, `responseStatusMetadata`, and validation bags) instead of exposing mutable endpoint internals by reference. Subscribed React/Vue/Svelte stores and caught client-validation errors can be treated as read models while mutations keep flowing through generated endpoint setters. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime; code that intentionally mutated `endpoint.state().data`, `endpoint.state().errors`, `endpoint.state().response`, `endpoint.state().responseMetadata`, `endpoint.state().responseStatusMetadata`, `endpoint.validationResult().errors`, or caught `FoundryValidationClientError.errors` to update the endpoint should switch to generated methods such as `setData(...)`, `setField(...)`, `setErrors(...)`, `setFieldErrors(...)`, `applyResponse(...)`, `resetData(...)`, or `resetErrors(...)`, or keep derived route metadata outside the endpoint snapshot.
- Generated TypeScript validation schema selectors now clone backend-owned metadata arrays/objects before returning schema fields, schema/root rules, nested rule rules/schema, rule values, messages, attributes, container lists, nullable-item lists, known fields, and strict-field lists. Dynamic form builders and validation docs can treat selector results as local read models without accidentally mutating generated validation contracts. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime; code that intentionally mutated `foundryValidationSchemaFields(...)`, `foundryValidationSchemaFieldRules(...)`, `foundryValidationRuleSchema(...)`, `foundryValidationSchemaMessages(...)`, `foundryValidationSchemaAttributes(...)`, or similar selector return values should keep that derived metadata in local state instead of relying on mutations to change the generated schema.
- Generated TypeScript validation schema metadata now includes count helpers for root/schema rules, field rules, rule values, field references, nested rules, schema fields, field-state fields, rule categories, field groupings, messages, attributes, containers, nullable items, and known/strict fields. Form builders, docs pages, and diagnostics can render backend-owned schema badges without local `.length` wrappers over generated metadata selectors. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime; replace local schema metadata count wrappers with helpers such as `foundryValidationSchemaFieldRuleCount(...)`, `foundryValidationSchemaFieldCountWithRuleCode(...)`, `foundryValidationRuleFieldReferenceCount(...)`, and `foundryValidationSchemaMessageCount(...)`.

Dynamic form sections and validation docs can branch on backend-owned schema metadata without local `count(...) > 0` or `.length > 0` wrappers. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime; replace local schema metadata presence wrappers with helpers such as `foundryValidationSchemaHasRules(...)`, `foundryValidationSchemaFieldHasRules(...)`, `foundryValidationSchemaHasFieldsWithRuleCode(...)`, `foundryValidationSchemaHasMessages(...)`, and `foundryValidationRuleHasValues(...)`.
- Generated TypeScript validation schema metadata now includes first-value helpers for schema rules, rule values, field references, nested rules, categorized schema/field rules, schema fields, field-state fields, field groupings, field-name groupings, rule-code groupings, messages, attributes, nullable items, known fields, and strict fields. Form builders and validation documentation screens can focus or preview the first backend-owned metadata item without local `[0]` access over generated selector arrays. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime; replace local first-item wrappers with helpers such as `foundryValidationSchemaFirstRule(...)`, `foundryValidationSchemaFieldFirstRule(...)`, `foundryValidationSchemaFirstFieldWithRuleCode(...)`, `foundryValidationSchemaFirstMessage(...)`, and `foundryValidationRuleFirstValue(...)`.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint instances now mirror backend-owned validation schema metadata through `validationSchema...` methods for schema/rule/field selectors, counts, presence checks, first values, rule-code groupings, messages, attributes, field labels, nullable/container metadata, known/strict fields, and unknown-field checks. Route-local form builders can stay on the endpoint object instead of wrapping `endpoint.validation` with local schema metadata helpers. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime; replace endpoint-local wrappers around `endpoint.validation` with methods such as `endpoint.validationSchemaFields()`, `endpoint.validationSchemaFieldRules(field)`, `endpoint.validationSchemaFirstFieldWithRuleCode(code)`, `endpoint.validationSchemaFirstMessage(field)`, and `endpoint.validationSchemaUnknownFields(data)`.
- Generated TypeScript route helpers now export route-specific validation metadata row aliases: `{RouteName}ValidationRule`, `{RouteName}ValidationField`, `{RouteName}ValidationMessage`, `{RouteName}ValidationAttribute`, and `{RouteName}ValidationContainer`. Dynamic form components can type backend-owned schema rows and endpoint `validationSchema...` method results without spelling generic `FoundryValidation*` types by hand. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime; replace local aliases such as `FoundryValidationField<{RouteName}RequestField>` with the generated route-specific aliases when sharing form metadata props.

- Generated TypeScript AppEnum metadata is now deep-frozen at runtime, including `{Enum}Values`, `{Enum}Options`, `{Enum}Meta`, string-backed `{Enum}Keys`, and grouped `{Enum}Groups`. - Generated TypeScript route helper endpoint `routeName` properties and metadata constants for HTTP method, request transport, and request media type now use `satisfies` instead of widening casts, preserving backend-owned literal types such as `"user.portal.login"`, `"post"`, `"body"`, or `"multipart/form-data"` while still checking them against Foundry's unions. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime; custom type assertions or snapshots that expected these values to be widened to the full union should accept the narrower generated literal types.

- Generated TypeScript endpoint instances and `state()` snapshots now expose `pendingSubmitCount` and `hasPendingSubmissions` from the same internal counter that drives `busy` / `processing`. Concurrent submit UIs, cancel controls, and debug panels can show active request counts without keeping a parallel counter. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime; custom stores or tests that manually construct `FoundryEndpointState` objects must include `pendingSubmitCount` and `hasPendingSubmissions` or derive state from `endpoint.state()`.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint `setErrors(...)` now replaces the whole generated error bag, so `setErrors({})` clears every field while `setFieldErrors(...)` remains the partial merge/update helper. Local form adapters can mirror a complete validation bag without stale fields from previous local or backend errors. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime; code that used `setErrors(...)` to merge a subset into existing errors should call `setFieldErrors(...)` instead.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint `clearErrors()` now matches Laravel-style no-argument behavior by clearing the whole generated error bag via `resetErrors()`, including backend-returned fields outside the generated field-state key list. Passing fields still clears only that variadic subset through `clearFieldErrors(...)`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime; UIs that intentionally used no-arg `clearErrors()` to clear only known generated fields should call `clearFieldErrors()` instead.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint submit attempts now clear stale `response`, `rawResponse`, and `status` at submit start, before client validation and network work. Pending UI no longer sees an older successful response as current while a new submit is in flight. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime; UIs that intentionally keep showing the previous response during a new submit should copy that payload into separate UI state before calling `submit(...)` / `submitForm(...)` / `submitResponse(...)`.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint instances now expose `clearResponse(...)` as a Laravel/Inertia-style alias for `resetResponse(...)`. Response body, raw status-aware response, documented status, and subscriber notification still flow through the existing backend-owned reset path. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime; adapters with local `clearResponse()` wrappers can call the generated endpoint directly.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint validation and server-error paths now clear stale success/response state when they apply errors. `validateForm(...)`, `validateFields(...)`, `applyValidationResult(...)`, `setFieldErrors(...)` / `setErrors(...)`, and `applyServerError(...)` no longer leave `wasSuccessful`, `recentlySuccessful`, `response`, `rawResponse`, or `status` from an older submit visible on an invalid endpoint. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime; UIs that intentionally display a previous success or response beside newly applied errors should copy that indicator/payload into separate UI state before applying the errors.

- Generated TypeScript endpoint instances now expose `clearProgress(...)`, and generated submit/error/success cleanup paths reuse one internal progress-clear state path. - Generated TypeScript endpoint `applyResponse(...)` now clears stale upload `progress` through the same shared success-state path as generated `submitForm(...)` / `submitResponse(...)`. - Generated TypeScript endpoint instances now expose Laravel-style `clearError(...)` / `clearErrors(...)` aliases beside `clearFieldError(...)` / `clearFieldErrors(...)`. `clearErrors()` clears the whole generated error bag, while `clearErrors("email", "password")` clears a variadic subset through the same nested/indexed/root-container path matching as the existing clear helpers. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; Laravel/Inertia-inspired form adapters with local `clearErrors(...fields)` wrappers can call the generated endpoint directly.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint instances now expose `setFieldError(...)` / `setFieldErrors(...)`, plus Laravel-style `setError(...)` / `setErrors(...)` helpers, for local/client validation errors. - Generated TypeScript endpoint instances and `state()` snapshots now keep the latest documented status-aware response envelope as `rawResponse: FoundryResponseByStatus<TResponses> | null`. Successful generated submits hydrate `response`, typed `rawResponse`, `status`, success flags, and recent-success state through one shared path, and custom success flows can call `applyResponse(response, { recentlySuccessfulDurationMs })`; `resetResponse()` clears stale response/status state with subscriber notification. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; custom stores or tests that manually construct `FoundryEndpointState` objects must include `rawResponse` or derive state from `endpoint.state()`, and local raw-response stores or direct `endpoint.response = null` / `endpoint.status = null` mutations can move to `state().rawResponse`, `applyResponse(...)`, and `resetResponse()`.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint instances now expose status-aware response helpers: `responseStatuses()`, `hasResponseStatus(...)`, `responseMetadataForStatus(...)`, and `hasDocumentedResponseStatus(...)`. `responseMetadataForStatus(...)` returns a cloned metadata object, the runtime also exports `FoundryResponseStatus<TResponses>`, and route helpers export `{RouteName}ResponseStatus` aliases derived from backend `response::<T>(status)` metadata. Status-aware screens can branch on route-specific status unions and inspect backend-owned `hasBody` / `mediaType` metadata without raw number checks or `responseMetadata.find(...)`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; replace local status unions, `endpoint.status === ...` helpers, and manual response metadata scans with the generated route status alias and endpoint helpers where status-aware UI state is backend-owned. - Generated TypeScript endpoint instances and `state()` snapshots now expose `hasResponse`, `hasServerError`, `hasErrorResponse`, and `hasValidationErrorResponse` presence booleans beside the nullable response/error payloads. - Generated TypeScript endpoint field-state selectors now include `foundryEndpointTouchedFieldStates(...)` / `foundryEndpointFirstTouchedFieldState(...)`, endpoint `touchedFieldStates(...)` / `firstTouchedFieldState(...)`, and matching `state().touchedFieldStates` / `state().firstTouchedFieldState` snapshot fields. - Generated TypeScript endpoint instances now expose `setInitialFields(...)` and `setInitialField(...)`, matching `setInitialData(...)` for partial saves. - Generated TypeScript endpoint instances now expose `resetFields(...)`, matching the bulk touch/validation/clear helpers. - Generated TypeScript endpoint instances now expose `clearFieldErrors(...)`, matching the existing bulk touch/validation helpers. Multi-step forms can clear a generated field subset, or the default generated field-state key list, in one state emission while preserving the same nested/indexed/root-container path matching as `clearFieldError(...)`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; replace local loops over `clearFieldError(...)` with `clearFieldErrors(...)` where step-level error clearing is backend-owned.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint `state()` snapshots now include `valid`, `invalid`, and `hasErrors`, derived from the same `validationResult()` as `state.validation`. Snapshot stores can branch on form validity without local `!state.validation.valid` aliases. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; custom stores or tests that manually construct `FoundryEndpointState` objects must include these fields or derive state from `endpoint.state()`.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint `state()` snapshots now include `invalidFieldStates`, `firstInvalidFieldState`, `visibleErrorFieldStates`, and `firstVisibleErrorFieldState`, derived once from the same generated `fieldStates` map. Snapshot subscribers can render summaries and touched/submitted visible-error lists without filtering the snapshot or calling back into the endpoint. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; custom stores or tests that manually construct `FoundryEndpointState` objects must include these derived fields or derive state from `endpoint.state()`.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint instances now expose `touchFields(...)` and `touchFieldsAndValidate(...)`, so multi-step forms can mark a generated field subset as touched, or touch and validate that subset, without local loops over `touchField(...)` / `validateFields(...)` or repeated subscriber notifications. `touchFields()` defaults to the same generated field-state key list used by `fieldStates()`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; replace local step-submit helpers that loop touched-state updates with the generated bulk helpers where touched and validation display state are backend-owned.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint instances now expose `touchFieldAndValidate(...)` and `touchFieldAndValidateDependents(...)`, combining touched-state updates with field or dependent-field validation in one emitted state update. Blur handlers can show touched-only validation errors without local `touchField(...)` + `validateField(...)` wrapper code or duplicate subscriber notifications. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; replace local blur helpers that touch and immediately validate a field with the generated combined methods where validation display state is backend-owned.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint instances now expose `setFieldAndValidate(...)` and `setFieldAndValidateDependents(...)`, combining typed field-path writes with field or dependent-field validation in one backend-owned change-handler call. The helpers avoid local `setField(...)` + `validateField(...)` / `validateFieldAndDependents(...)` wrapper code while preserving the same nested/indexed/root-container path contract. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; replace local input helpers that write a field and immediately validate it with the generated combined methods where validation state is backend-owned.
- Generated TypeScript validation dependency helpers now export `foundryValidationFieldReferenceMatches(...)`, and `foundryValidationRuleReferencesField(...)`, `foundryValidationSchemaFieldDependsOn(...)`, `foundryValidationSchemaFieldsReferencing(...)`, `foundryValidationSchemaFieldNamesReferencing(...)`, and endpoint `validateFieldAndDependents(...)` use the same nested/indexed/root-container path-family matching as validation field reads. Dependent-field refresh now covers cases like `children.name` vs. `children[0].name`, parent object changes vs. child references, and root-container paths such as `[0].email` / `items[0].email` vs. `email`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; remove local normalization around dependent-field maps that only existed to bridge schema field names and exact indexed/container runtime paths.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint instances now expose `validateFields(...)` and `validateFieldAndDependents(...)`. Form adapters can refresh a known field subset, or revalidate a changed field plus backend-owned sibling-rule dependents (`confirmed`, `required_if`, temporal comparisons, accepted/declined conditionals, etc.) without scanning validation metadata locally. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; change handlers that currently call `foundryValidationSchemaFieldNamesReferencing(...)` plus repeated `validateField(...)` calls can switch to `endpoint.validateFieldAndDependents(field)`.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint field-state defaults now use the exported `foundryValidationSchemaFieldStateFields(...)` selector, which unions generated schema fields with current validation error fields before building `fieldStates`, `invalidFieldStates(...)`, and `visibleErrorFieldStates(...)`. Server-only, unknown-field, and exact indexed backend error keys now stay visible in `state().fieldStates` without adapter-side key merging. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; if a UI intentionally needs only schema-declared fields, pass an explicit `foundryValidationSchemaFields(endpoint.validation).map((field) => field.name)` list or filter the generated state map.

Form adapters can render invalid summaries or touched/submitted visible-error lists without local filters over `fieldStates`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; replace local filters over generated field-state maps with the generated selectors where validation state is backend-owned.

Snapshot subscribers can render validation display state from the emitted object without calling `endpoint.fieldStates()` separately. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; custom stores or tests that manually construct `FoundryEndpointState` objects must include `fieldStates` or derive state from `endpoint.state()`.

- Generated TypeScript endpoint state now includes normalized upload `progress` (`loaded`, `total`, `progress`, `percentage`, `lengthComputable`), and submit options expose typed `onProgress(progress)`. Generated submits pass `config.onUploadProgress(event)` to the HTTP client, normalize native adapter events into endpoint state, forward them to `onProgress(...)`, and clear `progress` when the latest submit settles. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; custom upload form stores can switch to generated endpoint `progress`, and custom HTTP clients should call `config.onUploadProgress(event)` from their underlying Axios/fetch/upload implementation when progress is available.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint state now includes `recentlySuccessful`, a short-lived success pulse for save buttons and success banners. The latest successful submit sets it to `true`, it auto-clears after `recentlySuccessfulDurationMs` milliseconds from submit options (default 2000), and `resetSubmitState()` / new submit attempts clear any previous pulse. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; custom form stores that track local recently-successful timers can switch to generated endpoint state, and any manual `FoundryEndpointState` objects should include `recentlySuccessful`.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint submit options now expose typed lifecycle callbacks: `onStart(data)`, `onSuccess(response)`, `onError(error)`, and `onFinish()`, plus exported callback aliases such as `FoundrySubmitSuccessCallback<TResponses>`. Route-specific `{RouteName}SubmitOptions` aliases bind those callbacks to the generated request DTO and response map, so form adapters can run side effects without local submit wrapper types. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; custom form wrappers that wrap `submitForm(...)` / `submitResponse(...)` only to run submit lifecycle side effects can move that logic into the generated submit options.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint `submitForm(...)` and `submitResponse(...)` options now accept a typed `transform(data)` callback, and the runtime exports `FoundrySubmitTransform<TRequest>`. The transformed request payload is used for generated client-side validation, request media-type detection, multipart serialization, and query/body submission while leaving endpoint `data` unchanged. Generated route-specific `{RouteName}SubmitOptions` aliases bind the transform to that route's request DTO. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; custom submit wrappers that clone, trim, or normalize request data before calling generated endpoints can move that logic into the typed `transform` option.
- Generated TypeScript route helpers now export route-specific `{RouteName}State`, `{RouteName}StateSubscriber`, and `{RouteName}SubmitOptions` aliases, so React/Vue/Svelte adapters can import the exact backend-owned endpoint state and submit-option shapes without manually spelling `FoundryEndpointState<Request, Response, Params>` generics. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; custom form wrappers that currently define local route state or submit option aliases can switch to the generated aliases.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint instances now expose `validateField(...)`, and `FoundryEndpoint.ts` exports `validateFoundrySchemaField(...)`, letting form adapters run backend-owned client validation for one field without replacing unrelated field errors. Field validation also refreshes root container paths such as `[0].email`, descends into nested DTO paths such as `profile.name`, targets `each(nested)` item paths such as `children[0].name`, supports exact root map item paths such as `[tenant].email`, ignores malformed array/collection indexes instead of accidentally refreshing every item, and clears nested child errors when a parent field is cleared. Generated field reads now aggregate the same exact, nested, indexed, and root-container path families, `FoundryValidationClientError` exposes the same validation-result and field-read helpers as endpoint instances, and standalone validation result helpers accept `FoundryValidationFieldReadOptions` when custom stores need root container aggregation. Generated field parameters now preserve known nested and indexed field-path literals through `FoundryKnownFieldPath<T>`, while still accepting backend/server paths that are only known at runtime. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; custom blur/change validation code that currently calls `validateFoundrySchema(...)` for the whole form and manually merges one field can switch to `endpoint.validateField(...)` or `validateFoundrySchemaField(...)`, and catch blocks for client-side validation can call `error.firstError(...)` / `error.fieldCodes(...)` after narrowing to `FoundryValidationClientError`.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint `setField(...)` now accepts generated nested/indexed field paths through `FoundryFieldValue<TRequest, Field>`, so frontend adapters can write `profile.name`, `children[0].name`, root-array paths such as `[0].email`, collection item paths such as `items[0].email`, and exact root-map paths such as `[tenant].email` through the same backend-owned path contract used by validation, field reads, dirty checks, and resets. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; custom form wrappers with local path-setter utilities can switch nested/indexed writes to `endpoint.setField(...)`, while existing top-level `setField("email", value)` calls continue to work.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint instances now keep a clean request-data baseline through `initialData`, `setInitialData(...)`, `setInitialFields(...)`, `setInitialField(...)`, `isDirty(...)`, `isFieldDirty(...)`, `resetData(...)`, `resetFields(...)`, `resetField(...)`, and `FoundryEndpointState.dirty`, so frontend adapters do not need a parallel form-baseline store to implement dirty badges or reset buttons. `resetData(...)` clears generated validation/server-error state while restoring the clean value, `setInitialFields(...)` / `setInitialField(...)` mark generated field paths clean from current data, and `resetFields(...)` / `resetField(...)` restore generated field paths from `initialData` while clearing those paths' generated errors. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; React/Vue form wrappers that currently track their own initial DTO or per-field dirty/reset state can switch to the generated endpoint state and call `setInitialData()` after loading or saving fresh backend data.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint instances now expose touched-field state through `touched`, `FoundryTouchedFields<TRequest>`, `touchField(...)`, `isFieldTouched(...)`, and `resetTouched(...)`. Touched reads use the same nested, indexed, and root-container path matching as generated validation, field reads, dirty checks, and resets; `resetData(...)` clears all touched state, and `resetFields(...)` / `resetField(...)` clear touched state for those paths. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; custom React/Vue form wrappers with local touched maps can switch to generated endpoint state and helpers, and any code that manually constructs `FoundryEndpointState` objects should include `touched`.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint instances now expose submit lifecycle state through `submitted`, `submitCount`, `wasSuccessful`, `FoundryEndpointState` snapshots, and `resetSubmitState()`. `submitCount` increments for every generated submit attempt, including client-side validation failures, while `wasSuccessful` only follows the latest completed backend submit so concurrent older responses cannot mark the shared endpoint successful. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; custom form wrappers that track submitted/success state can switch to generated endpoint state, and any code that manually constructs `FoundryEndpointState` objects should include the new fields.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint instances now expose `applyServerError(...)`, letting custom adapters, wizard steps, and non-standard submit flows hydrate `serverError`, typed `errorResponse`, typed `validationErrorResponse`, `errors`, and `errorDetails` from a caught backend error through the same path used by generated `submitForm()` / `submitResponse()`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; custom form stores that currently call `foundryValidationResultFromError(error)` and manually copy server errors into endpoint-like state can switch to `endpoint.applyServerError(error)`.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint instances now expose `subscribeState(...)` plus `FoundryEndpointStateSubscriber` and `FoundryEndpointStateSubscriptionOptions`, letting frontend adapters subscribe directly to typed `endpoint.state()` snapshots and optionally receive the current snapshot immediately. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; custom React/Vue/Svelte form stores that currently wrap `endpoint.subscribe(() => endpoint.state())` can switch to `endpoint.subscribeState(...)`.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint instances now expose `state()` and the exported `FoundryEndpointState` type, giving React/Vue adapters a single typed snapshot of data, params, busy state, response/status, typed backend errors, generated field errors, and validation result. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; custom form hooks or stores that duplicate endpoint state interfaces can switch to `endpoint.state()` / `FoundryEndpointState<...>`.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint submit helpers now expose typed cancellation: `FoundryHttpRequestConfig.signal`, submit `signal`, submit `abortPrevious`, and endpoint `abortPending(reason?)`. Generated submits pass an `AbortSignal` to compatible HTTP clients, clean up abort listeners after settlement, and can cancel older in-flight submits before starting a new one. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; custom HTTP clients should forward `config.signal` to fetch/Axios so generated cancellation stops the network request. Existing code that passed `request.signal` keeps working, but `signal` is the preferred submit option.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint instances now sequence concurrent `submitForm()` / `submitResponse()` calls: `busy` stays true until every pending submit settles, while `response`, `status`, `serverError`, `errorResponse`, `validationErrorResponse`, `errors`, and `errorDetails` only update from the latest submit. Earlier slower requests still resolve or reject their own promises but no longer overwrite newer endpoint state. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; UI code that intentionally used an older in-flight submit to replace newer form state should move that behavior into local promise handling instead of relying on the shared endpoint instance state.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint submit helpers now accept top-level `query` options for extra URL query values and reject `options.request.params` on query-transport submissions, keeping backend-owned DTO query fields separate from adapter params while still forwarding `request.params` for body/form submissions. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; callers that used `submitForm({ request: { params } })` or `submitResponse({ request: { params } })` to add query values to GET/HEAD typed DTO endpoints should move those values to `query` or `route: { query }`.
- Generated TypeScript `createRouteUrlBuilder(...)` now merges builder-level `query` defaults with per-call route query values instead of replacing the whole query object, preserving shared filters or tenant hints while still letting a route call override individual keys. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; if code intentionally relied on per-call `query` dropping every builder-level query key, set those keys to `undefined` in the per-call query or construct a builder without query defaults.
- Generated `FoundryEndpoint.ts` now exports `validateFoundrySchema(...)`, `assertFoundrySchemaValid(...)`, `foundryValidationResultFromError(...)`, `emptyFoundryValidationResult()`, `foundryValidationFirstMessage(...)`, `foundryValidationFieldCodes(...)`, and other validation result/error-bag utilities, and route endpoint `validateForm()` / server-error handling use those same shared runtime paths. Endpoint instances also expose `setField(...)`, `validationResult()`, `hasErrors()`, `firstError(...)`, `fieldCodes(...)`, `clearFieldError(...)`, and `applyValidationResult(...)`, and `validateForm()` / `applyValidationResult(...)` / submissions clear stale backend error envelopes before replacing generated field errors. Submissions also clear stale generated field errors before sending the next request. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; custom Vue/React form hooks can import a generated `{RouteName}Validation` constant with `validateFoundrySchema(...)`, normalize Foundry 422 responses with `foundryValidationResultFromError(...)`, update and clear a single edited field with `setField(...)` or clear without changing data with `clearFieldError(...)`, and read field messages/codes from either results or `FoundryValidationClientError` or a generated endpoint instance with generated helpers instead of copying validation logic. If a form intentionally displayed previous backend envelopes after applying a new validation result or after a new client-side validation failure, or previous field errors while submitting with `validate: false`, keep those messages in local UI state instead of relying on the generated endpoint error bag.
- `TsValidationRule` now has typed constructors for common no-argument and control rules such as `required()`, `email()`, `nullable()`, `numeric()`, `accepted()`, `date()`, `distinct()`, `each([...])`, and `nested(child_schema)`, reducing stringly manual validation metadata. Existing `TsValidationRule::new(...)` usage remains supported.
- Fluent validators and manual TypeScript validation metadata now expose `min_length(...)` and `max_length(...)` aliases that emit the canonical `min` / `max` rule codes, matching `#[derive(Validate)]` alias behavior. Existing `min(...)` / `max(...)` usage is unchanged.
- `TsValidationRule::app_enum::<E>()` now publishes manual validation metadata from `FoundryAppEnum::accepted_keys()`, including aliases and integer-backed enum keys, matching `#[validate(app_enum(E))]` without copying enum values by hand. **Consumer follow-up:** manual validators that currently build `TsValidationRule::new("app_enum").values(...)` can switch to the typed helper and regenerate frontend types/OpenAPI docs.
- `TsValidationRule::custom(ValidationRuleId::new("..."))` now publishes typed server-only custom rule metadata with the same `code` and `params.rule` shape as `#[validate(rule(...))]`, so manual validators can share rule ids with backend registration.
- `types:export` now emits `ValidationRuleManifest.ts` from registered custom validation rules, including grouped `ValidationRuleIds` and `serverOnly: true` metadata for frontend form builders/docs. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; custom forms/tooling can replace copied backend rule names with `ValidationRuleManifest` / `ValidationRuleIds`.
- `ValidationRuleManifest.ts` now includes `validationRuleNames()`, `validationRuleEntries()`, and `serverOnlyValidationRules()`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; form builders and validation docs tooling can replace copied custom-rule lists and server-only filters with the generated selectors.
- `types:export` now emits `PluginManifest.ts` from registered plugins, including plugin ids, versions, Foundry version constraints, dependencies, contribution counts, asset target paths/kinds, scaffold variables/files, and grouped `PluginIds`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; admin/dev tooling can replace copied plugin metadata with `PluginManifest` / `PluginIds`.
- `PluginManifest.ts` now includes `pluginEntries()`, `pluginHasDependencies(...)`, `pluginsWithAssets(...)`, `pluginsWithScaffolds()`, `pluginContributionCount(...)`, and `pluginsWithContribution(...)`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; plugin dashboards can replace copied asset/scaffold/contribution filters with the generated selectors.
- `PluginManifest.ts` now includes `pluginNames()`, `pluginsWithDependencies()`, `pluginNamesWithDependencies()`, `pluginAssetKinds()`, `isPluginAssetKind(...)`, `pluginNamesWithAssets(...)`, `pluginNamesWithScaffolds()`, `pluginContributionNames()`, `isPluginContributionName(...)`, and `pluginNamesWithContribution(...)`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; plugin dashboards can replace local plugin-name maps, asset-kind guards, and contribution-name guards with generated selectors.

- `HttpManifest.ts` now includes `httpCsrfTokenFromCookie(...)`, `httpCsrfHeaders(...)`, and `HttpCsrfHeaderMap`, derived from the configured CSRF cookie/header names. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; browser clients can replace hand-written `document.cookie` parsing and hard-coded `X-CSRF-Token` headers with `httpCsrfHeaders(document.cookie)`.
- `HttpManifest.ts` now includes safe CORS, security-header, CSRF, and rate-limit selectors such as `httpCorsAllowedMethods()`, `httpCorsAllowedHeaders()`, `httpSecurityHeadersEnabled()`, `httpRateLimitMaxRequests()`, `httpRateLimitWindowSeconds()`, and `httpRateLimitBy()`, plus `HttpRateLimitMaxRequests`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; HTTP diagnostics/admin clients can replace copied CORS, security-header, and global rate-limit config reads with generated helpers.
- `HttpManifest.ts` now includes `HttpRateLimitByValues`, `isHttpRateLimitBy(...)`, `httpRateLimitByValues()`, `httpCorsAllowsMethod(...)`, and `httpCorsAllowsHeader(...)`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; browser clients and diagnostics dashboards can replace copied rate-limit mode guards and CORS allow-list checks with generated helpers.
- `types:export` now emits `NotificationManifest.ts` and a `TsNotification` registration surface for backend-owned broadcast notification payload DTOs, including `NotificationPayloadMap`, `TypedNotificationBroadcastPayload`, built-in `NotificationChannelIds`, canonical `NotificationBroadcastChannel` / `NotificationBroadcastEvent` constants, and helpers such as `isTypedNotificationBroadcastPayload()`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; apps can register notification payload DTOs and replace hand-written broadcast notification `data` interfaces, copied notification channel names, and copied WebSocket notification channel/event strings with generated exports.
- `NotificationManifest.ts` now includes `notificationTypes()` and `notificationChannelNames()` so notification dashboards and clients can list backend-owned notification types and built-in channel ids without reading raw manifest constants. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; replace local `Object.keys(NotificationManifest)` / `Object.values(NotificationChannelIds)` helpers with the generated selectors.
- `NotificationManifest.ts` now includes `isNotificationPayloadName(...)`, `notificationTypesWithPayload(...)`, and `notificationUsesPayload(...)` so notification dashboards and broadcast handlers can validate/group payload schemas from backend-owned metadata. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; replace local notification payload-name guards and payload-to-type maps with the generated helpers.
- `NotificationManifest.ts` now includes `NotificationPayloadName`, `notificationEntries()`, `notificationPayloadNames()`, and `notificationsWithPayload(...)`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; notification dashboards can replace copied notification type/payload grouping code with the generated selectors.
- `NotificationManifest.ts` now includes delivery-channel and broadcast selectors/predicates such as `notificationEmailChannelName()`, `notificationBroadcastDeliveryChannelName()`, `notificationBroadcastChannel()`, `notificationBroadcastEvent()`, `notificationChannelIsBroadcast(...)`, `notificationIsBroadcastChannel(...)`, and `notificationIsBroadcastEvent(...)`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; notification preference screens and WebSocket broadcast handlers can replace copied channel/event string comparisons with generated selectors.
- `types:export` now adds safe WebSocket runtime config to `WebSocketChannelManifest.ts`, including `WebSocketRuntimeManifest`, `WebSocketPath`, heartbeat timings, query-token metadata, client-facing limits, history caps, and `webSocketUrl()`, while omitting bind host/port, allowed origins, and transport buffer internals. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; socket clients can replace copied WebSocket path/query-token/heartbeat constants with `WebSocketRuntimeManifest`, `WebSocketPath`, and `webSocketUrl()`.
