- `WebSocketChannelManifest.ts` now includes runtime selectors (`webSocketPath()`, `webSocketHeartbeat()`, `webSocketLimits()`, `webSocketQueryToken()`, `webSocketHistory()`) and channel selectors such as `webSocketChannelManifestEntry()`, `webSocketChannels()`, `webSocketPresenceChannels()`, `webSocketClientEventChannels()`, `webSocketChannelsRequiringAuth()`, `webSocketPublicChannels()`, `webSocketChannelHasPermission()`, `webSocketChannelClientEvents()`, and `webSocketChannelServerEvents()`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; socket clients, channel pickers, and WebSocket dashboards can replace copied runtime reads and `Object.values(WebSocketChannelManifest)` scans with generated helpers.
- `WebSocketChannelManifest.ts` now includes channel-name selectors, permission filters, client-event channel guards, and event allow-list helpers such as `webSocketChannelNames()`, `webSocketPresenceChannelNames()`, `webSocketClientEventChannelNames()`, `webSocketChannelsWithPermission(...)`, `isWebSocketClientEventChannelName(...)`, `webSocketChannelAllowsClientEvent(...)`, and `webSocketChannelAllowsServerEvent(...)`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; WebSocket clients and dashboards can replace copied channel-name maps, permission filters, and client/server event allow-list checks with generated helpers.
- WebSocket app events can now register backend-owned payload DTOs with `TsWebSocketPayload::server(...)` and `TsWebSocketPayload::client_event(...)`; `types:export` adds `WebSocketPayloadManifest`, payload maps, typed app-server frame aliases, and `typedClientEventToChannel()` to `WebSocketChannelManifest.ts`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; apps with custom socket payload interfaces can register the Rust DTOs and switch frontend code to the generated payload maps/typed frame helpers.
- `types:export` now emits `JobManifest.ts` from the app's registered job runtime and safe job config, including job ids, resolved queues, grouped `JobIds`, `JobRuntimeManifest`, retry/timeout/concurrency policy, queue priorities, history-retention metadata, and optional `TsJobPayload` DTO maps while omitting worker polling, lease, requeue, shutdown, and prune scheduling internals. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; dashboards and internal tooling can replace copied job id/queue/runtime policy strings with `JobManifest`, `JobIds`, and `JobRuntimeManifest`, and can register job payload DTOs when they need typed payload inspection.
- `JobManifest.ts` entries now include each job's resolved `queuePriority`, plus a `jobPriority(name)` helper, derived from the backend queue-priority config already exported in `JobRuntimeManifest`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; job dashboards can read `jobPriority(...)` or `JobManifest[name].queuePriority` instead of joining job queues to `JobRuntimeManifest.queuePriorities` manually.
- `JobManifest.ts` now includes `JobQueueName`, `JobPayloadName`, `jobEntries()`, `jobQueueNames()`, `jobsInQueue(...)`, `jobsWithQueuePriority()`, `jobPayloadName(...)`, `jobHasPayload(...)`, and `jobsWithPayload(...)`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; job dashboards can replace copied queue/payload/priority filters with the generated selectors.
- `JobManifest.ts` now includes `isJobPayloadName(...)`, `jobNames()`, `jobPayloadNames()`, `jobNamesWithPayload(...)`, and `jobUsesPayload(...)`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; job dashboards can replace local `Object.keys(JobManifest)`, payload-name guards, and payload-to-job maps with the generated helpers.
- `JobManifest.ts` now includes `isJobQueueName(...)`, `jobNamesInQueue(...)`, and `jobUsesQueue(...)`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; job dashboards can replace local queue-name guards and queue-to-job-name maps with the generated helpers.
- `types:export` now emits `EventManifest.ts` from registered event listeners plus optional `TsEventPayload` DTO metadata, including grouped `EventIds`, listener counts, and event payload maps. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; dashboards/plugins can replace copied event strings with `EventManifest` / `EventIds`, and event payload DTOs can be registered even before listeners exist.
- `EventManifest.ts` now includes `EventPayloadName`, `eventEntries()`, `eventPayloadName(...)`, `eventHasPayload(...)`, `eventsWithPayload(...)`, `eventsWithListeners()`, and `eventsWithoutListeners()`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; event dashboards and plugin tooling can replace copied payload/listener grouping filters with the generated selectors.
- `EventManifest.ts` now includes `isEventPayloadName(...)`, `eventNames()`, `eventPayloadNames()`, `eventNamesWithPayload(...)`, and `eventUsesPayload(...)`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; event dashboards and plugin tooling can replace local `Object.keys(EventManifest)`, payload-name guards, and payload-to-event maps with the generated helpers.
- `EventManifest.ts` now includes `eventNamesWithListeners()` and `eventNamesWithoutListeners()`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; event dashboards and plugin tooling can replace local listener-state event-name maps with the generated helpers.
- `types:export` now emits `ScheduleManifest.ts` from registered scheduler tasks and scheduler config, including cron expressions or interval milliseconds, overlap-lock flags, environment filters, hook presence, grouped `ScheduleIds`, and `SchedulerRuntimeManifest` with tick interval, leadership lease TTL, and shutdown timeout. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; admin/scheduler tooling can replace copied schedule ids, timing metadata, and scheduler runtime policy with `ScheduleManifest`, `ScheduleIds`, and `SchedulerRuntimeManifest`.
- `ScheduleManifest.ts` now includes `ScheduleEnvironmentName`, `ScheduleHookName`, `scheduleEntries()`, `cronSchedules()`, `intervalSchedules()`, `scheduleEnvironments(...)`, `scheduleHasEnvironment(...)`, `schedulesForEnvironment(...)`, `scheduleUsesOverlapLock(...)`, `schedulesWithoutOverlapping()`, `scheduleHasHook(...)`, and `schedulesWithHook(...)`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; scheduler dashboards can replace copied kind/environment/hook/overlap filters with the generated selectors.
- `ScheduleManifest.ts` now includes `scheduleNames()`, `cronScheduleNames()`, `intervalScheduleNames()`, `scheduleEnvironmentNames()`, `isScheduleEnvironmentName(...)`, `scheduleNamesForEnvironment(...)`, `scheduleNamesWithoutOverlapping()`, `scheduleHookNames()`, `isScheduleHookName(...)`, and `scheduleNamesWithHook(...)`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; scheduler dashboards can replace local schedule-name maps, environment/hook guards, and name-only filters with generated selectors.
- `types:export` now emits `CommandManifest.ts` from the running CLI command registry, including command ids, descriptions, argument counts, subcommand counts, and grouped `CommandIds`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; admin/dev tooling can replace copied command strings with `CommandManifest` / `CommandIds`.
- `CommandManifest.ts` now includes registered CLI argument names and subcommand names in addition to the existing counts, so admin/dev tooling can inspect backend-owned command shape without scraping Clap output. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; existing `argCount` / `subcommandCount` consumers keep working and can opt into `arguments` / `subcommands` when needed.
- `CommandManifest.ts` now includes `CommandArgumentName`, `CommandSubcommandName`, `commandEntries()`, `commandArguments(...)`, `commandSubcommands(...)`, `commandHasArgument(...)`, `commandHasSubcommand(...)`, `commandsWithArguments()`, and `commandsWithSubcommands()`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; admin/dev tooling can replace copied argument/subcommand filters with the generated selectors.
- `CommandManifest.ts` now includes `commandNames()`, `commandArgumentNames()`, `commandSubcommandNames()`, `isCommandArgumentName(...)`, `isCommandSubcommandName(...)`, `commandNamesWithArgument(...)`, and `commandNamesWithSubcommand(...)`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; admin/dev tooling can replace local command argument/subcommand guards and command-name maps with generated selectors.
- `make:ids` now scaffolds a starter `ids.rs` module with `FoundryId` guard and route enums plus an `AppEnum` ability enum backed by `PermissionId`, so app-owned semantic ids can live in one backend module while ability values remain exportable to TypeScript. **Consumer follow-up:** import the generated enum variants where guards, permissions, or named routes are referenced; regenerate frontend types if clients use the generated ability enum metadata.
- `make:model` now scaffolds models with `serde::Serialize`, Foundry re-exported `ts_rs::TS`, and `ApiSchema` derives alongside `Model`, so fresh models can be used as generated TypeScript/OpenAPI response contracts without adding direct `ts-rs` or `serde_json` dependencies; it also avoids the previous duplicate `Clone` implementation from deriving `Clone` next to `Model`. **Consumer follow-up:** newly scaffolded models are auto-registered for `types:export`; regenerate frontend types after adding one, or remove `ApiSchema`/`ts_rs::TS` from a generated model if it is intentionally backend-only. Crates that used `make:model` without already depending on `serde` should add `serde = { version = "1", features = ["derive"] }`, matching the existing generated job scaffold.
- `make:request` now scaffolds typed request DTOs with `serde::Deserialize`, Foundry re-exported `ts_rs::TS`, `ApiSchema`, and `Validate`, so fresh request contracts are ready for `JsonValidated<T>` / `Validated<T>`, generated TypeScript route helpers, and OpenAPI validation metadata without adding a direct `ts-rs` dependency. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/OpenAPI docs after adding a scaffolded request; crates that use the scaffold need the existing `serde = { version = "1", features = ["derive"] }` dependency.
- `make:response` now scaffolds typed response DTOs with `serde::Serialize`, Foundry re-exported `ts_rs::TS`, and `ApiSchema`, so fresh response contracts are ready for `route.response::<T>(status)`, `types:export`, and OpenAPI route docs without adding a direct `ts-rs` dependency. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/OpenAPI docs after adding a scaffolded response; crates that use the scaffold need the existing `serde = { version = "1", features = ["derive"] }` dependency.
- `make:guard` now scaffolds auth guards with a backend-owned `GuardId`, a `register(...)` helper, and a `BearerAuthenticator` implementation shell that uses Foundry's `async_trait` re-export. A trailing `Guard` suffix is removed from the generated id, so `ApiGuard` registers `GuardId::new("api")`, and registered guards flow into `AuthManifest.ts` / `AuthGuardIds` without copying guard ids into frontend code. **Consumer follow-up:** implement the generated `authenticate(...)` body, add the matching `[auth.guards.<id>]` config entry, call the generated `register(registrar)?` helper from a service provider, and regenerate frontend types when clients rely on guard ids.
- `make:policy` now scaffolds auth policies with a backend-owned `PolicyId`, a `register(...)` helper, and a `Policy` implementation shell that uses Foundry's `async_trait` re-export, so registered policies flow into `AuthManifest.ts` / `AuthPolicyIds` without copying policy ids into frontend code. **Consumer follow-up:** implement the generated `evaluate(...)` body, call the generated `register(registrar)?` helper from a service provider, and regenerate frontend types when clients rely on policy ids.
- `make:job` now scaffolds jobs with Foundry re-exported `ts_rs::TS` and `foundry::TS` derives alongside `serde::Serialize` / `Deserialize`, so fresh job payload structs are exportable without adding a direct `ts-rs` dependency. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types after adding a scaffolded job; when dashboards or tooling need `JobPayloadMap` to reference it, add a `TsJobPayload::new(JobId::new("..."), "JobType")` inventory entry after registering the job. Remove the TS derives only for intentionally backend-only jobs.
- `make:event` now scaffolds typed domain events with a backend-owned `EventId`, `Event` impl, TypeScript/OpenAPI derives, and `TsEventPayload` registration, so fresh event payloads appear in `EventManifest.ts` without copying event strings into frontend tooling. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types after adding a scaffolded event; existing hand-written events can adopt the same derives and `TsEventPayload::new(...)` inventory entry when dashboards or plugins need typed event payloads.
- `make:notification` now scaffolds typed notifications with a backend-owned notification type constant, `Notification` impl, TypeScript/OpenAPI derives, database/broadcast payload renderers, and `TsNotification` registration, so fresh broadcast notification payloads appear in `NotificationManifest.ts` without copying notification strings into frontend clients. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types after adding a scaffolded notification; existing hand-written notifications can adopt the same derives and `TsNotification` inventory entry when broadcast clients need typed `NotificationBroadcastPayload.data` narrowing.

### Changed

- `doctor --deploy --strict` now treats pending migrations as a warning, which makes strict deploy gates fail until `db:migrate` has applied the registered migration set. Missing applied migrations still fail immediately as drift. **Consumer follow-up:** run `db:migrate` before strict doctor checks, or use non-strict `doctor --deploy --json` when intentionally inspecting a pre-migration package.
- Generated TypeScript unknown-field selectors now preserve request-field typing: `foundryValidationSchemaUnknownFields(...)` and endpoint `validationSchemaUnknownFields(...)` return `readonly FoundryRequestField<TRequest>[]` instead of plain `readonly string[]`, while still returning the same container-prefixed unknown paths. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime; update TypeScript snapshots or explicit annotations that expected `readonly string[]`.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint instance field-reference helpers now preserve `FoundryRequestField<TRequest>` return types for `validationSchemaFieldRuleFieldReferences(...)`, `validationSchemaFieldFirstRuleFieldReference(...)`, `validationSchemaFieldReferences(...)`, and `validationSchemaFieldFirstReference(...)`, matching the already-typed standalone helpers instead of widening the facade to plain `string`. Runtime values are unchanged. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime; update TypeScript snapshots or explicit facade method typings that expected `readonly string[]` / `string | undefined`.
- App-backed `types:export` and built-in OpenAPI spec generation now check explicit custom validation metadata (`#[validate(rule(...))]` and `TsValidationRule::custom(...)`) against the runtime validation rule registry before writing generated frontend files or caching the observability OpenAPI spec, including apps with no registered custom rules. Manual custom metadata must also use the same registered id for the rule `code` and `params.rule`. Built-in server-only validation metadata is unchanged. **Consumer follow-up:** if export or OpenAPI bootstrap fails with an unregistered or inconsistent validation rule, register the referenced custom rule with `AppBuilder::register_validation_rule(...)` in the app used for type export/docs, or replace hand-written custom metadata with `TsValidationRule::custom(MY_RULE_ID)` before regenerating frontend types/OpenAPI clients.
- Generated TypeScript DTO validation comments now render explicit custom validation metadata as `rule(id) [server]` instead of only the raw rule id, matching Rust's `#[validate(rule(...))]` syntax while keeping generated metadata keyed by the registered rule id. **Consumer follow-up:** update snapshots or doc tests that assert generated validation comments for custom rules.
- `Country` now exposes its known JSON-backed metadata as typed Rust fields (`currencies: Vec<CountryCurrency>`, `calling_suffixes`, `tlds`, and `timezones` as `Vec<String>`) and generated TypeScript now exports `Country` / `CountryCurrency` alongside `CountryStatus`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types and update Rust code that treated those fields as `serde_json::Value` to use the typed vectors directly; no migration changes are required because the PostgreSQL columns remain raw JSON.
- Auth guide examples now use `FoundryId` for guard ids instead of hand-written `From<Guard>` implementations, matching the fixture app and reducing duplicated guard string mappings.
- TypeScript guide examples and missing-route-schema diagnostics now recommend `foundry::ts_rs::TS` plus `#[ts(crate = "foundry::ts_rs")]`, matching generated scaffolds and avoiding a direct `ts-rs` dependency for consumer DTO exports. **Consumer follow-up:** existing DTOs that derive `ts_rs::TS` can keep working, or switch to `foundry::ts_rs::TS` with the `#[ts(crate = "foundry::ts_rs")]` attribute if the app does not otherwise need a direct `ts-rs` dependency.
- Generated migration, seeder, guard, policy, and job scaffolds now use `#[foundry::async_trait]` through Foundry's root re-export instead of importing `async_trait::async_trait` directly. **Consumer follow-up:** existing generated files can keep their direct `async-trait` dependency, or switch imports to `#[foundry::async_trait]` and remove `async-trait` if nothing else uses it. Raw SQL migration bodies are unchanged.
- Notification rustdoc now uses typed `NotificationChannelId` constants in `via()` examples instead of stale string vectors.

### Fixed

- Direct `RouteManifestEntry` TypeScript export now rejects blank or padded guard ids, permission ids, route docs text, and tags; duplicate permissions/tags per route; and duplicate `operationId` values across the manifest, matching the normalized registrar/OpenAPI route metadata contract before frontend helpers are generated. **Consumer follow-up:** no change for routes registered through Foundry's HTTP registrar; trim/drop blank direct manifest docs metadata and dedupe hand-built permissions, tags, and operation ids before regenerating frontend route helpers.
- Generated core config manifests now fail fast before emitting malformed frontend metadata: `AppManifest` rejects blank/padded app identity and unsafe background shutdown timeout numbers, `AuditManifest` exports backend-normalized/deduplicated sensitive field names, and `LoggingManifest` rejects padded or control-character log directories while preserving documented empty-directory and zero-retention sentinels. **Consumer follow-up:** keep `app.name` and custom `app.environment` trimmed and non-blank, update strict audit snapshots that expected raw sensitive field names such as `cardToken` instead of `card_token`, and keep non-empty `logging.log_dir` trimmed before regenerating frontend config helpers.
- Generated `SettingManifest` export now validates select/multiselect option metadata before writing frontend form helpers, rejecting missing or empty option arrays, malformed option rows, blank/padded labels, and duplicate option values that would make `settingOptionForValue(...)` ambiguous. **Consumer follow-up:** update `SettingDefinition::select(...)` and `SettingDefinition::multiselect(...)` registrations to provide non-empty `parameters.options` arrays of `{ value, label }` objects with unique values and trimmed labels before regenerating frontend setting helpers.
- Generated `EventManifest` export now rejects per-event listener counts and aggregate listener totals above TypeScript's safe integer range before writing frontend event helpers. **Consumer follow-up:** normal registered listeners are unchanged; lower impossible hand-built `EventDescriptor.listener_count` values in direct tests or fixtures before regenerating frontend event helpers.
- Generated `AuthRuntimeManifest` export now uses backend-effective auth config for trimmed bearer prefixes, lowercase session cookie SameSite values, lockout clamps, MFA pending-token TTL/recovery-code clamps, and blank-MFA-issuer fallback to `app.name`; it also rejects invalid direct runtime metadata such as blank/padded guard ids, bad bearer prefixes, invalid session cookie settings, zero TTLs, unsafe TypeScript numbers, and duplicate MFA required roles. **Consumer follow-up:** trim `auth.bearer_prefix`, keep token/session/reset/email/MFA TTLs greater than `0`, keep session cookie settings valid (`same_site = "none"` requires secure cookies), and update strict generated snapshots that expected raw padded prefixes, raw uppercase SameSite values, or zero lockout/MFA clamp values before regenerating frontend auth helpers.
- Generated `HttpManifest` export now uses backend-effective HTTP config for security-header fallbacks, normalized CSRF header names, and lowercase CSRF cookie SameSite values; preserves documented `0` sentinels for disabled global body-size caps and request timeouts; and rejects invalid direct runtime metadata such as unsafe TypeScript numbers, invalid CSRF cookie/header settings, wildcard-origin CORS credentials, duplicate CORS allow-list values, enabled global rate-limit zero values, and global `by = "actor"` rate limits. **Consumer follow-up:** keep CSRF cookie/header settings valid, do not combine `allowed_origins = ["*"]` with `allow_credentials = true`, dedupe CORS allow lists, keep enabled global rate limits positive, use `actor_or_ip` globally and route-level `by_actor()` after auth, and update strict generated snapshots that expected raw uppercase CSRF header names or padded/uppercase SameSite values before regenerating frontend HTTP helpers.
- Generated `ObservabilityManifest` export now uses the same backend-normalized observability base path as route registration and HTTP sampling exclusion; it adds missing leading slashes, trims trailing slashes, preserves documented `0` retention sentinels, and rejects invalid direct runtime metadata such as unsafe TypeScript numbers, non-literal base paths, and blank or padded service names. **Consumer follow-up:** keep `observability.base_path` as a literal normalized path, keep `observability.service_name` non-blank and trimmed, lower extremely large retention values before regenerating frontend observability helpers, and update strict snapshots that expected raw base paths such as `ops/`.
- Generated `CacheManifest` export now uses backend-effective distributed remember-lock TTL/poll clamps, preserves documented `key_max_length = 0` and disabled-lock timing sentinels, and rejects cache timing/limit values above TypeScript's safe integer limit plus memory cache `max_entries = 0`. **Consumer follow-up:** keep memory cache capacity greater than `0`, lower extremely large cache timing/limit values before regenerating frontend cache helpers, and update strict generated snapshots that expected enabled distributed-lock TTL or poll intervals of `0`.
- Direct `WebSocketChannelDescriptor` TypeScript export now rejects blank or padded channel ids, guard ids, permission ids, and declared event ids; duplicate channel ids; and duplicate permissions per channel, matching the registrar's backend-owned WebSocket manifest shape before frontend socket helpers are generated. **Consumer follow-up:** no change for channels registered through Foundry's WebSocket registrar; trim hand-built descriptor metadata and dedupe direct descriptor ids/permissions before regenerating frontend socket helpers.
- Generated `WebSocketRuntimeManifest` export now rejects config values that would otherwise drift from server behavior: blank/padded or relative `websocket.path`, zero heartbeat interval/timeout values, zero `history_buffer_size`, invalid enabled query-token names, and exported numeric runtime values above TypeScript's safe integer range. **Consumer follow-up:** set `websocket.path` to a trimmed `/...` path, keep `heartbeat_interval_seconds`, `heartbeat_timeout_seconds`, and `history_buffer_size` greater than `0`, keep exported WebSocket runtime numbers within JavaScript's safe integer range, and use a query-token name without whitespace, control characters, or `& = ? #` before regenerating frontend socket helpers.
- Generated `JobRuntimeManifest` export now rejects config values that would otherwise drift from server behavior: blank or padded `jobs.queue`, blank or padded `jobs.queue_priorities` keys, zero `jobs.max_retries`, zero `jobs.timeout_seconds`, and exported timeout/concurrency values above TypeScript's safe integer range. **Consumer follow-up:** set job queue names to trimmed non-empty ids, keep `jobs.max_retries` / `jobs.timeout_seconds` greater than `0`, and keep exported job runtime numbers within JavaScript's safe integer range before regenerating frontend job helpers; `max_concurrent_jobs = 0` and `history_retention_days = 0` remain valid unlimited/keep-forever sentinel values.
- Direct `ScheduleManifest` TypeScript export now rejects unparseable cron expressions, zero interval schedules, interval milliseconds above TypeScript's safe integer limit, zero scheduler tick intervals, and zero scheduler leader lease TTL values, matching the parsed scheduler registrar and runtime clamp contract before frontend scheduler helpers are generated. **Consumer follow-up:** no change for normal registered cron/interval schedules; fix hand-built schedule descriptors with invalid cron or zero/unsafe intervals, and keep `scheduler.tick_interval_ms` / `scheduler.leader_lease_ttl_ms` greater than `0` before regenerating frontend scheduler helpers. `scheduler.shutdown_timeout_ms = 0` remains the documented abort-immediately sentinel.
- Generated `StorageRuntimeManifest` export now rejects config values that would otherwise drift from backend storage behavior: blank or padded configured default disks, direct descriptor default-disk mismatches, upload/runtime numbers above TypeScript's safe integer limit, per-file upload caps above enabled total caps, zero enabled temp/orphan maintenance intervals, and unsafe attachment orphan prefixes. **Consumer follow-up:** trim `storage.default`, ensure hand-built disk descriptors mark the configured default disk, keep per-file upload caps within any non-zero total cap, use positive prune intervals when temp/orphan maintenance is enabled, and keep `attachment_orphan_prefix` as a safe relative storage prefix before regenerating frontend storage helpers. Documented `0` sentinels for upload caps, temp retention, and image decode caps remain valid.
- Generated `EmailRuntimeManifest` export now rejects config values that would otherwise drift from backend mailer behavior: blank or padded configured default mailers, blank or padded email queue names, direct descriptor default-mailer mismatches, attachment limits above TypeScript's safe integer limit, and per-file attachment caps above enabled total caps. **Consumer follow-up:** trim `email.default` and `email.queue`, ensure hand-built mailer descriptors mark the configured default mailer, and keep `max_attachment_bytes` within any non-zero `max_total_attachment_bytes` before regenerating frontend email helpers. `max_attachment_bytes = 0` and `max_total_attachment_bytes = 0` remain valid no-cap sentinels.
- Generated `DatabaseManifest` export now emits the effective backend pagination defaults after the same positive clamp used by the direct `Pagination` extractor, and rejects direct pagination defaults that are zero or above TypeScript's safe integer limit. **Consumer follow-up:** strict snapshots that expected `database.default_per_page = 0` to generate `DatabaseDefaultPerPage = 0` should be updated to `1`, and hand-built database manifest descriptors should use positive safe-integer defaults before regenerating frontend pagination helpers.
- Generated `DatatableRuntimeManifest` export now rejects `datatable.max_per_page` and `datatable.max_export_rows` values above TypeScript's safe integer limit, preventing table builders and export dialogs from receiving precision-losing caps. **Consumer follow-up:** lower extremely large datatable caps before regenerating frontend datatable helpers, or use `0` for the documented unlimited sentinel.
- Upload validation allow-lists now reject blank or padded MIME / extension values in both `#[derive(Validate)]` literals and manual `TsValidationRule` metadata, preventing generated TypeScript/OpenAPI upload contracts that can never match real browser files. **Consumer follow-up:** trim or remove blank values in `allowed_extensions(...)`, `allowed_mimes(...)`, `TsValidationRule::allowed_extensions([...])`, and `TsValidationRule::allowed_mimes([...])`; generated metadata from valid rules is unchanged.
- Manual TypeScript validation export now shape-checks backend-owned server-only built-ins instead of accepting malformed metadata. `unique` / `exists` require `table` and `column`, `allowed_mimes` requires values, dimensions require integer `width` / `height`, `after_hook` requires a non-empty hook id, and server-only `regex` / `not_regex` patterns must still be valid Rust regexes; unknown custom server-only rule ids remain free-form. **Consumer follow-up:** no change for generated metadata or typed helpers; fix hand-written server-only built-in metadata that was missing required params, values, or valid regex patterns.
- Manual TypeScript validation metadata now rejects array `size` rules with non-integer values when `kind = "array"`, matching the backend `Vec<T>` / `Option<Vec<T>>` collection length contract and `TsValidationRule::size_items(n)` helper. **Consumer follow-up:** no change for generated metadata or typed helpers; hand-written `TsValidationRule::new("size").param("kind", "array")` rules must use a non-negative integer `size`.
- `#[derive(Validate)]` and `#[derive(ApiSchema)]` now parenthesize validation rule expressions before stringifying metadata values, so negative numeric literals such as `in_list(-1)`, `not_in(-1)`, `min_numeric(-10.5)`, and `gt(-20.0)` compile and export correctly. **Consumer follow-up:** no migration required; DTOs that avoided negative validation literals by using string workarounds can switch back to numeric literals and regenerate frontend/OpenAPI artifacts.
- `#[derive(Validate)]` now renders sibling field values through the same typed presence semantics used for field-local validation, so cross-field rules such as `required_if`, `required_with`, `required_with_all`, `required_without`, `required_without_all`, `prohibits`, and default `confirmed` compile and validate correctly when the referenced sibling is `Option<T>`, `Option<Vec<T>>`, maps, JSON values, uploaded files, or nested DTOs. **Consumer follow-up:** no migration required; DTOs that avoided optional sibling validation rules by adding shadow string fields can remove those workarounds and regenerate frontend/OpenAPI artifacts.
- Derived and manual OpenAPI validation constraints now keep JSON Schema enum values type-correct for numeric fields. `in_list(...)`, `not_in(...)`, and raw numeric fields validated against int-backed `app_enum(E)` emit numeric enum values instead of stringified numbers; raw string fields with `#[validate(app_enum(E))]` use `FoundryAppEnum::accepted_keys()`, so declared aliases appear in generated request constraints, while typed AppEnum fields keep their canonical enum schema. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate OpenAPI clients/docs; strict snapshots for raw string `app_enum` fields with aliases, numeric `in_list`/`not_in`, or raw numeric `app_enum` fields may need updating.
- `#[derive(Validate)]` now supports `app_enum(E)` on string/numeric fields and `each(app_enum(E))` on string/numeric collections without trying to treat those values as the enum type first. The emitted validation metadata uses `FoundryAppEnum::accepted_keys()`, so declared AppEnum aliases are accepted by backend validation and generated frontend prevalidation. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime; remove local string-to-enum validation workarounds where DTOs intentionally keep raw request keys.
- Generated TypeScript `validateFoundrySchema(...)` and `validateFoundrySchemaField(...)` now compute `valid` from both `errors` and `errorDetails`, matching `foundryValidationHasErrors(...)`, endpoint validation snapshots, and `foundryValidationResultFromError(...)`. Detail-only validation bags can no longer appear valid after generated schema execution. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime; remove local guards that recompute generated schema-validation validity from `errorDetails`.
- Backend validation and generated TypeScript validation prevalidation now resolve indexed nested paths through the same unindexed base metadata fallback. Custom messages, custom attributes, and i18n keys registered for paths such as `addresses.streetName` now apply to indexed errors such as `addresses[0].streetName`, instead of only collapsing to the collection root. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime; remove local validation path-normalization workarounds that strip indexes before looking up backend-owned message or attribute metadata.
- Generated field-level validation message helpers now read `errorDetails` messages when a validation bag has detailed errors without a parallel `errors` message map. `foundryValidationFieldMessages(...)`, `foundryValidationFirstMessage(...)`, endpoint `fieldMessages(...)` / `firstError(...)`, and `FoundryValidationClientError` field reads no longer return empty field messages for details-only custom stores. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; remove local field-level fallback code that maps `fieldDetails(...)` to messages before rendering validation errors.
- Generated validation summary message helpers now read `errorDetails` messages when a validation bag has detailed errors without a parallel `errors` message map. `foundryValidationErrorMessages(...)`, `foundryValidationFirstErrorMessage(...)`, endpoint `errorMessages()`, and `firstErrorMessage()` no longer return empty summaries for details-only custom stores. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; remove local fallback code that maps `errorDetails` to messages before rendering validation summaries.
- Generated `foundryValidationResultFromError(...)` now preserves `errorDetails` from generated validation error bags and `FoundryValidationClientError` inputs, so rule codes are not collapsed to `invalid` when custom stores normalize an already-generated validation result. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; remove workaround code that reattaches `errorDetails` after calling `foundryValidationResultFromError(...)` on generated client validation errors.
- `#[derive(AppEnum)]` now emits `serde` and `serde_json` references through Foundry's root re-exports, so generated app enum/typed-id modules can compile in consumer crates without adding those direct dependencies solely for the macro expansion. **Consumer follow-up:** crates that only kept `serde` or `serde_json` for `AppEnum` can remove those dependencies after updating; keep them if request/response DTOs or app code use their derives, types, or helpers directly.
- `#[derive(Validate)]` now emits JSON parsing and JSON-object key validation helpers through Foundry's re-exported `serde_json` path instead of requiring consumer crates to depend on `serde_json` only because of validation macro expansion. **Consumer follow-up:** crates that only added `serde_json` for `Validate` derive expansion can remove that direct dependency after updating; keep it if app code names `serde_json::Value`, `json!`, or other `serde_json` APIs directly.
- `#[derive(Validate)]` now generates multipart extractor impls through Foundry's re-exported `axum` path instead of requiring consumer crates to depend on `axum` directly. **Consumer follow-up:** crates that only added `axum` because `Validate` derived DTOs failed to compile can remove that direct dependency after updating.
- `Pagination` now implements a direct Axum extractor that reads `database.default_per_page` from `AppContext` when `per_page` is omitted, and exposes config-aware helpers for manual construction. Existing `Query<Pagination>` handlers keep the serde fallback of `15` because query deserialization has no app state. **Consumer follow-up:** switch handlers from `Query(page): Query<Pagination>` to `pagination: Pagination` when endpoint defaults should follow backend config; snapshot tests for omitted `per_page` may need updating after that opt-in change.
- `Paginated::links()`, `Paginated::to_response()`, `Paginated::map_response()`, and `ApiResource::paginated()` now preserve existing query parameters, replace stale `page` / `per_page` values, and keep URL fragments when generating `next` / `prev` links. **Consumer follow-up:** update snapshot tests or clients that expected the old malformed `...?filter=x?page=2&per_page=...` style links; filtered paginated endpoints should pass the current request URL as the base.
- WebSocket `ack`, `presence:join`, and `presence:leave` protocol payloads now have backend-owned Rust DTOs (`WebSocketAckPayload`, `WebSocketAckStatus`, `WebSocketPresenceJoinPayload`, and `WebSocketPresenceLeavePayload`) with generated TypeScript exports, and `WebSocketChannelManifest.ts` reuses those DTOs instead of duplicating inline payload aliases. Existing JSON output is unchanged. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types and replace hand-written ACK/presence protocol payload interfaces or custom `"ok" | "error"` unions with the generated types.
- Validation now supports `required_keys(...)` for string-keyed maps and JSON object fields, including manual `Validator::keys(...).required_keys(...)`, manual `TsValidationRule::required_keys(...)` metadata, `#[derive(Validate)]`, generated TypeScript route-helper prevalidation, and OpenAPI object `required` + `x-foundry-validation` metadata. `Option<HashMap<...>>` / `Option<BTreeMap<...>>` fields skip absent values unless paired with a presence rule, while present empty maps still validate. **Consumer follow-up:** after adding `required_keys(...)` to DTOs, regenerate frontend types and OpenAPI clients/docs so forms and schema tooling see the backend-owned key contract.
- Generated WebSocket protocol error payloads now alias the backend-owned `ErrorResponse` contract, and WebSocket rate-limit error frames include the standard `status: 429` field. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; custom socket clients or tests that synthesize `WebSocketErrorPayload` must include `status`, and code that duplicated the old loose error shape can import `ErrorResponse` / `WebSocketErrorPayload` instead.
- `AuthError` now builds its HTTP and WebSocket error payloads from the standard `ErrorResponse` DTO and exposes `AuthError::response_body()` for custom guards that need the typed body. Existing JSON output is unchanged.
- WebSocket handshake HTTP rejections, missing request-id extractor failures, OpenAPI-spec misses, and WebSocket observability `404` branches now serialize through the backend-owned `ErrorResponse` contract; generated OpenAPI also documents `404 ErrorResponse` for `/_foundry/ws/presence/{channel}` and `/_foundry/ws/history/{channel}`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate OpenAPI clients/frontend types; dashboards that read `error` from WebSocket observability `404` bodies should read `message` and `status` from `ErrorResponse` instead.
- CSRF token helper payloads now have a backend-owned `CsrfTokenResponse` DTO, generated TypeScript export, and public prelude export; built-in CSRF, rate-limit, maintenance-mode, body-limit, timeout, and CORS rejection bodies now reuse the standard `ErrorResponse` contract instead of anonymous JSON. Existing JSON output is unchanged. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types if SPAs expose or consume a CSRF-token helper route, and prefer `CsrfTokenResponse` / `ErrorResponse` over hand-written `{ token }` or `{ message, status }` interfaces.
- Guarded routes now add framework-owned `401` and `403` `ErrorResponse` contracts to generated OpenAPI docs, and to the generated TypeScript route manifest when the route already has a typed request or response contract. Runtime responses are unchanged. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate OpenAPI clients/frontend types; status-aware route helpers may now expose additional `401` / `403` branches for guarded endpoints.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint helpers now expose thrown backend validation envelopes as `validationErrorResponse: ValidationErrorResponse | null` while keeping the existing `errorResponse`, `errors`, and `errorDetails` behavior. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime; form UIs that need the raw 422 envelope can read `endpoint.validationErrorResponse` instead of casting `serverError` or `errorResponse.errors`.
- Validation failures now serialize through a backend-owned `ValidationErrorResponse` DTO, generated TypeScript exports that exact 422 envelope alongside `FieldError`, and routes can document the standard 422 contract with `.validation_errors()` instead of spelling the DTO manually. The JSON response shape remains `{ message, status, errors }`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/OpenAPI clients; routes that want status-aware validation clients should use `.validation_errors()` or keep an existing explicit 422 response if they intentionally return a custom envelope.
- Custom `#[validate(rule(...))]` validators now appear in generated TypeScript and OpenAPI validation metadata as server-only rules keyed by their registered rule id, for example `{ code: "mobile", serverOnly: true }`, instead of being hidden behind generic or missing metadata. Runtime validation is unchanged. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/OpenAPI clients; tooling that inspected generated custom validation rules as `code: "rule"` should read the actual custom rule id and can keep using `params.rule` during migration.
- Struct-level `#[validate(after(...))]` hooks now appear in generated TypeScript and OpenAPI validation metadata as schema-level server-only rules, for example `{ code: "after", params: { hook: "validate_signup" }, serverOnly: true }`. Runtime validation is unchanged. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/OpenAPI clients; tooling that inspects route validation schemas should account for optional top-level `rules` on generated validation schemas.
- OpenAPI query endpoints now preserve request schema-level validation metadata, such as `#[validate(after(...))]`, on the operation-level `x-foundry-validation` extension when the request DTO is expanded into query parameters. Field-local query validation metadata remains on each parameter schema. Runtime behavior is unchanged. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate OpenAPI docs/clients if GET/HEAD DTOs use schema-level validation hooks.
- Manual `RequestValidator` DTOs can now publish generated TypeScript route-helper and OpenAPI request-schema validation metadata with fluent `TsValidationSchema` / `TsValidationField` / `TsValidationRule` builders and a `TsValidation` inventory entry, matching the metadata shape emitted by `#[derive(Validate)]`. Runtime validation is unchanged. **Consumer follow-up:** manual validators that currently duplicate form rules in frontend code or OpenAPI tooling can register the backend-owned schema and regenerate frontend types/OpenAPI docs.
- Manual `TsValidationSchema` metadata now projects supported built-in validation helpers into normal OpenAPI JSON Schema constraints, including required arrays/query parameter flags, string length/pattern rules, array item rules, numeric bounds, enums/not-in, embedded `nested` child schemas, strict `deny_unknown_fields()` object contracts, `each(...)` item constraints, and upload vendor extensions. Runtime behavior is unchanged. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate OpenAPI clients/docs if manual validators rely on frontend schema tooling.
- The manual validation metadata types (`TsValidation`, `TsValidationSchemaProvider`, `TsValidationSchema`, `TsValidationField`, `TsValidationRule`, `TsValidationMessage`, and `TsValidationAttribute`) are now re-exported from `foundry::prelude::*`, matching other app-facing framework extension points. **Consumer follow-up:** manual validator metadata code can replace `foundry::typescript::...` imports with the prelude when convenient.
- Validation docs now publish the implementation-derived 89-feature field/collection rule surface instead of the old 38-rule snapshot, and clearly keep file upload validation documented as a separate derive/file-helper surface. A guard test keeps the README, guide index, API index, and validation guide aligned with the backend `FieldRule` implementation.
- `types:export` now rejects generated TypeScript artifacts that reuse an exported name or target the same `.ts` output file instead of letting one export overwrite another and leaving the barrel/route-helper schema map ambiguous. This covers type contracts, AppEnum files/helper names, route helper exports, the barrel, and Foundry runtime manifest files; duplicate identical registrations for the same type/path remain idempotent. **Consumer follow-up:** give each `foundry::TS` / `ApiSchema` type a valid unique TypeScript name and unique `#[ts(export_to = "...")]` path that does not overlap AppEnum names/helpers, framework-owned names/files, or route helpers, or remove redundant manual `TsType` registrations before regenerating frontend types.
- `types:export` now rejects duplicate or malformed manual `TsAppEnum` metadata before writing generated enum files, including invalid export names, blank ids, empty options, `keyKind`/value mismatches, duplicate option values, and blank label keys. **Consumer follow-up:** keep one `TsAppEnum` entry per enum, use valid Rust/TypeScript type names, provide at least one backend enum option, and keep option values/labels aligned with `FoundryAppEnum::meta()`.
- `types:export` and fallible OpenAPI generation now reject duplicate `TsValidation` schema names instead of silently letting inventory order decide validation metadata. The new `try_generate_openapi_spec(...)` API returns those generation errors, and the built-in OpenAPI observability route setup propagates them during HTTP bootstrap. **Consumer follow-up:** keep exactly one validation metadata registration per DTO; remove a manual `TsValidation` entry if the same DTO also derives `Validate`, or move all metadata into the manual registration.
- `types:export` and fallible OpenAPI generation now reject malformed manual `TsValidationSchema` metadata, including blank or whitespace-padded field names, rule codes, rule parameter keys, message field/rule keys, attribute field keys, blank custom messages, and blank attribute labels. **Consumer follow-up:** trim manual validation metadata keys and provide visible custom message/attribute text before regenerating frontend types or OpenAPI docs.
- Manual `TsValidationSchema` metadata now rejects unknown non-server-only rule codes instead of exporting rules that the generated TypeScript validator silently skipped. **Consumer follow-up:** mark custom, async, and database-backed manual rules with `.server_only()`, or add generated TypeScript runtime support before exposing them as client-checkable rules.
- Manual schema-level `TsValidationSchema::rule(...)` entries now must be server-only because generated TypeScript client validation only executes field-level rules today. **Consumer follow-up:** add `.server_only()` to manual schema-level hooks/rules such as `after`, or move genuinely browser-checkable constraints into `.field(...)` metadata.
- Manual `TsValidationSchema` message and attribute metadata now rejects unknown field names, and messages also reject rule names that are not reachable from that field's client-side rule tree. **Consumer follow-up:** fix typos in `.message(field, rule, ...)` / `.attribute(field, ...)`, keep custom messages aligned with field rules or `each(...)` item rules, and regenerate frontend types/OpenAPI docs.
- Manual client-checkable `TsValidationRule` metadata now rejects underspecified params/values, such as `min` without `min`, `between` without `min`/`max`, `required_keys` without values, or prefix/suffix/contains rules without `value` or `values`. **Consumer follow-up:** fill in the same params/values that derive-generated metadata emits, or mark backend-only/manual rules with `.server_only()`.
- Manual client-checkable `TsValidationRule` metadata now rejects extra params, values, nested rules, or schemas that its generated TypeScript runtime case ignores. **Consumer follow-up:** remove stale manual metadata keys/values, move real constraints into the matching rule shape, or mark backend-only metadata with `.server_only()`.
- Manual client-checkable `each` and `nested` metadata now rejects no-op shapes: `each` must include at least one nested item rule, and `nested` must include a child validation schema. **Consumer follow-up:** add `.nested_rule(...)` / `.nested_rules(...)` to manual `each` metadata, add `.schema(...)` to manual `nested` metadata, or mark intentionally backend-only control metadata with `.server_only()`.
- Manual client-checkable `TsValidationRule` metadata now rejects malformed numeric and UUID params, such as non-integer `min`, non-finite `min_numeric`, non-positive `multiple_of`, or `uuid` versions outside `1..=8`. **Consumer follow-up:** normalize manual rule params to the same shapes derive-generated metadata emits, or mark backend-only/manual rules with `.server_only()`.
- Client-checkable validation metadata now rejects impossible numeric ranges, such as `decimal`, `digits_between`, or `between` rules where `min > max`, before generating TypeScript/OpenAPI contracts. **Consumer follow-up:** swap or correct invalid range bounds in `#[validate(...)]` attributes or manual `TsValidationRule` params before regenerating frontend types/OpenAPI docs.
- Manual client-checkable `regex` / `not_regex` metadata now rejects patterns that are not valid Rust regexes before generating TypeScript/OpenAPI contracts. **Consumer follow-up:** fix malformed manual `pattern` params or mark intentionally backend-only regex-like checks with `.server_only()`.
- Derived `regex` / `not_regex` rules that use Rust regex syntax Foundry cannot safely translate to JavaScript now export as server-only TypeScript/OpenAPI validation metadata instead of silently no-oping in browser prevalidation or emitting overconfident OpenAPI `pattern` constraints. Manual client-checkable regex metadata now rejects those browser-incompatible patterns. **Consumer follow-up:** mark manual Rust-only regex rules with `.server_only()`, or rewrite the pattern to the browser-compatible subset before regenerating frontend types/OpenAPI docs.
- Manual `TsValidationRule` metadata for field-list rules (`required_with_all`, `required_without_all`, and `prohibits`) now rejects `params.other` values that do not match the joined `values` list, and new helper constructors fill both from one source. **Consumer follow-up:** replace hand-built field-list rule metadata with `TsValidationRule::required_with_all(...)`, `required_without_all(...)`, or `prohibits(...)`, or keep `params.other` equal to `values.join(", ")`.
- Manual value-list `TsValidationRule` metadata for rules such as `starts_with`, `ends_with`, and `contains` now rejects `params.value` values that do not match the joined `values` list, preventing generated validation messages from describing a different contract than the browser runtime checks. **Consumer follow-up:** omit `params.value` when using `values(...)`, or keep it equal to `values.join(", ")`.
- Manual cross-field `TsValidationRule` metadata now rejects blank or whitespace-padded field references in `params.other` and field-list `values`, matching derive-generated serde wire field names. **Consumer follow-up:** trim manual `other` params and field-list values for rules such as `required_if`, `confirmed`, `required_with_all`, and `prohibits` before regenerating frontend types/OpenAPI docs.
- Generated TypeScript client validation now evaluates `contains` rule `values` for both collection-style metadata and manual metadata instead of only using `params.value` on string values. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime if manual `TsValidationRule::new("contains").values(...)` metadata exists; browser prevalidation will now require every listed value to be present, matching backend collection `contains_all` semantics.
- Generated TypeScript validation messages now derive `{{value}}` from rule `values` for prefix/suffix/contains rules when `params.value` is absent, and derive `{{keys}}` for `required_keys` from its values list. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/runtime if custom client-side validation messages interpolate these placeholders from manual values-only metadata.
- OpenAPI generation now rejects duplicate normalized method/path docs and duplicate `operationId` values instead of letting later routes overwrite earlier generated client contracts. **Consumer follow-up:** remove duplicate route docs or give intentionally separate routes distinct paths, methods, or operation ids.
- OpenAPI component schema insertion now rejects conflicting schemas that share the same `ApiSchema::schema_name()` instead of letting the later schema overwrite the earlier component. Identical component reuse, such as `String` across many routes, is still accepted. **Consumer follow-up:** give distinct Rust DTOs unique schema names when their JSON shapes differ, especially for manually implemented `ApiSchema`.
- OpenAPI component schema names are now validated before `$ref` generation; component names must be non-empty and contain only ASCII letters, digits, dots, hyphens, or underscores. **Consumer follow-up:** update manual `ApiSchema::schema_name()` implementations that return names with spaces, slashes, generic brackets, or other punctuation to a stable OpenAPI-safe name.
- OpenAPI generation and route manifest collection now reject duplicate response schemas for the same status on one route instead of allowing response/status maps to overwrite one contract with another. **Consumer follow-up:** keep one `response::<T>(status)` per route status; use one envelope/enum DTO when a status can return multiple domain shapes.
- OpenAPI generation, route manifest collection, and direct TypeScript route manifest export now reject documented response statuses outside the valid HTTP `100-599` range; direct TypeScript route manifest export also rejects duplicate response statuses per route, matching registrar-collected routes. **Consumer follow-up:** replace invalid `response::<T>(status)` / hand-built `RouteManifestResponse.status` values such as `99` or `700` with valid HTTP statuses, and keep one response schema per status.
- OpenAPI generation now rejects documented routes that have no response metadata, preventing invalid operations with no `responses` object. **Consumer follow-up:** add at least one `response::<T>(status)` or `validation_errors()` call to request-only route docs before regenerating OpenAPI.
- Route doc text metadata (`method`, `operationId`, `summary`, `description`, and `tags`) is now trimmed at the `RouteDoc` source, blank metadata is ignored, and route tags stay first-seen unique. Generated OpenAPI operations and TypeScript route manifest entries no longer repeat tags or preserve accidental surrounding whitespace, and fallible OpenAPI generation now rejects direct/internal route-doc metadata that still contains blank, padded, or duplicate document fields. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate OpenAPI docs/frontend types if custom tooling reads route metadata; duplicated tag entries collapse to one entry in original order, whitespace-only `operationId` overrides fall back to the named route id, and hand-built route docs should use trimmed unique metadata before generation.
- OpenAPI generation, route manifest collection, and direct TypeScript route manifest export now reject documented HTTP methods outside Foundry's supported method set (`get`, `post`, `put`, `patch`, `delete`, `head`, `options`) instead of emitting invalid OpenAPI operation keys or TypeScript literals that do not satisfy `RouteHttpMethod`. The generated `RouteHttpMethod` union now renders from the backend-owned method list. **Consumer follow-up:** replace manual `RouteDoc::method(...)` / hand-built `RouteManifestEntry.method` values such as `fetch` with a supported method, or add a typed framework route method before documenting it.
- Direct TypeScript route manifest export now rejects blank or whitespace-padded request and response schema names before writing `RouteManifest.ts` or endpoint helper metadata. **Consumer follow-up:** ensure hand-built `RouteManifestEntry.request` and `RouteManifestResponse.schema` values are non-empty, trimmed schema names such as `UserResponse`, `Array<UserResponse>`, or `Unit`.
- Direct TypeScript route manifest export now rejects invalid schema atoms such as `Admin/User Response` and malformed or unsupported generic schema expressions such as `Array<>` or `Envelope<UserResponse>`; schema atoms must use OpenAPI-safe characters and generic schema metadata must use Foundry-supported wrappers (`Array<T>`, `Map<T>`, `Nullable<T>`, `PaginatedResponse<T>`, `CursorPaginated<T>`, or `Collection<T>`). **Consumer follow-up:** update hand-built `RouteManifestEntry.request` / `RouteManifestResponse.schema` values to use plain OpenAPI-safe DTO schema names or supported wrappers before regenerating frontend types.
- Direct TypeScript route manifest export now rejects blank, whitespace-padded, or relative `RouteManifestEntry.path` values before writing URL helpers. **Consumer follow-up:** use backend-style absolute paths such as `/users/{id}` in hand-built route manifest entries.
- Direct TypeScript route manifest export now rejects `RouteManifestEntry.params` that do not exactly match the params declared by `RouteManifestEntry.path`, preventing generated URL helper types from accepting stale or incomplete route params. **Consumer follow-up:** keep hand-built route manifest params in backend path order, or prefer registrar-collected route manifests so params are derived from the route path.
- Direct TypeScript route manifest export now rejects auth metadata where `guard` or `permissions` are populated while `requires_auth` is false, preventing frontend route guards from treating protected routes as public. **Consumer follow-up:** for hand-built `RouteManifestEntry` values with guard or permission metadata, set `requires_auth` to true; dynamic-authorizer routes can still use `requires_auth: true` without guard or permissions.
- Direct TypeScript route manifest export now rejects request transport/media metadata that does not match backend-collected route manifests: no request metadata without a request schema, no body media type for query transport, and body transport must include a media type. **Consumer follow-up:** for hand-built `RouteManifestEntry` values, set `request_transport`/`request_media_type` from the same request schema decision the backend route collector would make, or prefer registrar-collected manifests.
- Direct TypeScript route manifest export now rejects `RouteManifestResponse.has_body` and `RouteManifestResponse.media_type` values that do not match Foundry's backend status/schema response metadata rules. **Consumer follow-up:** for hand-built `RouteManifestResponse` values, derive `has_body` from status plus schema (`204` / `205` / `304` and `Unit` are bodyless) and derive `media_type` from the schema (`UploadedFile` roots are `application/octet-stream`, bodyless responses are `None`, others are JSON), or prefer registrar-collected manifests.
- `TsValidationSchema::field(...)` now merges rules into an existing field with the same name instead of emitting duplicate field entries, exact duplicate schema/nested rules and duplicate rule values are ignored by the fluent builders, and duplicate `.message(field, rule, ...)` / `.attribute(field, ...)` calls now replace the existing entry. This keeps manually composed validation metadata deterministic. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/OpenAPI docs if a manual validation schema intentionally chained repeated field/rule/value/message/attribute calls; field rules and first-seen unique values are preserved in call order under one entry, while duplicate messages/attributes use the last builder call.
- Generated OpenAPI now documents the job observability JSON endpoints (`/_foundry/jobs/stats` and `/_foundry/jobs/failed`) with stable operation ids and backend-owned `JobsStatsResponse` / `JobsFailedResponse` schemas, including `JobHistoryStatus` enum values and required nullable failed-job metadata fields. Existing JSON output is unchanged. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate OpenAPI clients/docs if dashboards consume job observability routes.
- Generated OpenAPI now documents the core observability JSON endpoints (`/_foundry/health`, `/_foundry/ready`, and `/_foundry/runtime`) with stable operation ids and backend-owned `LivenessReport`, `ReadinessReport`, and `RuntimeSnapshot` schemas. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate OpenAPI clients/docs if operations tooling consumes these observability routes.
- Generated OpenAPI now documents the SQL observability JSON endpoint (`/_foundry/sql`) with the backend-owned `SqlObservabilitySnapshot`, `SqlObservabilityStats`, `SlowQueryEntry`, and `NPlusOneSuspect` schemas. Existing JSON output is unchanged. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate OpenAPI clients/docs if dashboards consume SQL observability.
- Generated OpenAPI now documents the built-in WebSocket observability JSON endpoints (`/_foundry/ws/channels`, `/_foundry/ws/presence/{channel}`, `/_foundry/ws/history/{channel}`, and `/_foundry/ws/stats`) with stable operation ids and backend-owned response schemas, including required nullable `guard` / `room` fields. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate OpenAPI clients/docs if dashboards consume the `/_foundry/ws/*` observability routes.
- Generated TypeScript now protects and documents WebSocket observability response contracts (`WebSocketChannelsResponse`, `WebSocketPresenceResponse`, `WebSocketHistoryResponse`, `WebSocketStatsResponse`, and their nested row/counter records), so admin dashboards can consume backend-owned `/_foundry/ws/*` response shapes instead of duplicating them locally. Existing JSON output is unchanged. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types and replace hand-written WebSocket observability interfaces with the generated contracts.
- WebSocket channel protocol event ids (`subscribed`, `unsubscribed`, `presence:join`, and `presence:leave`) are now reserved end to end: channel registration, backend publishing, client-event relay, and generated TypeScript frame guards no longer accept those ids as arbitrary app events. Framework protocol frames are unchanged. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types and rename any custom server/client events that reused those Foundry protocol ids to domain-specific event names.
- Direct TypeScript WebSocket channel manifest export now rejects descriptor metadata that cannot come from the backend registry: guard/permission metadata with `requires_auth: false`, `client_events` while `allow_client_events` is false, duplicate declared events, and reserved protocol event ids in app client/server event lists. **Consumer follow-up:** for hand-built `WebSocketChannelDescriptor` values, mirror registry output or prefer registrar-collected descriptors.
- OpenAPI schemas for `DatatableJsonResponse` now document backend-owned datatable column, pagination, filter, applied-filter, sort, and `Collection<T>` shapes instead of opaque or duplicated object placeholders. JSON output and generated TypeScript names are unchanged. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate OpenAPI clients/docs if they read datatable response metadata schemas.
- Route docs for `Collection<T>` now preserve the item type in the generated route manifest, TypeScript endpoint aliases (`{ items: T[] }`), generated client-side request validation for collection `items`, and inline OpenAPI response/request schemas instead of collapsing to an opaque `Collection` name. Runtime JSON remains `{ items: [...] }`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/OpenAPI clients for endpoints documented with `request::<Collection<T>>()` or `response::<Collection<T>>(...)`; replace hand-written `{ items: ... }` aliases with the generated route helper type where possible, and expect client-side validation errors for collection requests to use paths such as `items[0].email`.
- GET/HEAD typed request transport now only auto-expands plain non-wrapper, non-file object DTOs whose fields are scalar values or scalar arrays into query parameters. Wrapper request schemas such as `request::<Collection<T>>()`, nested object DTOs, and DTOs containing `UploadedFile` stay body/multipart requests in OpenAPI, the route manifest, and generated TypeScript endpoint helpers. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/OpenAPI clients; if a GET/HEAD endpoint intentionally accepted collection, nested object, or upload data through query params, model that contract as an explicit flat scalar query DTO instead of relying on wrapper/nested/file DTO expansion.
- OpenAPI request bodies for direct `request::<UploadedFile>()` and `request::<Vec<UploadedFile>>()` route roots now document the actual multipart field used by generated TypeScript helpers: `{ file: binary }` or repeated `file` parts. Nullable direct roots (`Option<UploadedFile>` / `Option<Vec<UploadedFile>>`) document `file` as optional. DTOs containing file fields are unchanged. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate OpenAPI clients/docs for direct-file endpoints; generated client call shapes may move from a top-level binary/array body to a multipart object with a `file` property, matching the existing route helper default unless callers override `formDataField`.
- OpenAPI responses and generated route manifest metadata for `response::<UploadedFile>(...)`, `response::<Vec<UploadedFile>>(...)`, and nullable `Option<_>` wrappers around those file roots now use `application/octet-stream` instead of `application/json`, matching the generated TypeScript `File` / `File[]` aliases. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/OpenAPI clients for file download endpoints; custom route manifest consumers should accept `RouteResponseMediaType` value `"application/octet-stream"` and configure HTTP clients for binary/blob responses where needed.
- Generated TypeScript route helpers now export `{RouteName}ResponseMetadata` and endpoint instances expose `responseMetadata`, reusing the backend-owned `RouteManifestResponse[]` shape with `status`, `schema`, `hasBody`, and `mediaType`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; custom classes that extend `FoundryEndpoint` directly should implement `readonly responseMetadata` or extend the generated endpoint helper class.
- Generated TypeScript `validateForm()` now stops evaluating later rules for a field after `required`, `filled`, or a prohibited/prohibits rule fails, matching backend validation's terminal presence-rule behavior instead of showing extra client-side errors such as `email` / `min` for an already-empty or already-prohibited field. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; form UIs that counted every client-side rule error for terminal presence failures should expect the backend-aligned single error.
- Generated TypeScript `validateForm()` now checks `#[validate(size(...))]` on numeric DTO fields with the same tolerant exact-number comparison as Rust `size_numeric`, instead of requiring strict JavaScript number equality. String and collection `size` behavior is unchanged. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; numeric values produced by normal floating-point calculations may no longer show a frontend-only `size` error when the backend would accept them.
- Generated TypeScript validation metadata for collection `#[validate(size(...))]` now includes `params.kind = "array"`, and `validateForm()` uses it to require an array with the exact item count instead of allowing a non-array value with the same string length. The validation error code remains `size`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; custom tooling that exact-matches `size` params should tolerate the additional `kind` key.
- OpenAPI schemas now mark `#[validate(json)]` on parsed JSON fields such as `serde_json::Value` as server-only `x-foundry-validation` metadata, matching generated TypeScript route helpers, while string JSON fields continue to use `format: "json-string"`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate OpenAPI docs/clients; custom validation metadata readers should skip server-only `json` rules for already-parsed JSON values.
- OpenAPI and generated route manifest docs now treat `std::collections::HashSet<T>` like `Vec<T>` / `BTreeSet<T>`, emitting array schemas and `Array<T>` route aliases for direct request/response roots. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate OpenAPI docs/frontend types for endpoints documented with `HashSet` roots; local wrapper DTOs used only to document unique arrays can be removed.
- Manual TypeScript validation schemas now expose collection exact-size rules through the canonical backend `code: "size"` plus `kind: "array"` metadata. `TsValidationRule::size_items(n)` emits that shape directly, and legacy `TsValidationRule::new("size_items").param("size", n)` entries are normalized before export. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types if manual `TsValidationSchema` entries used `size_items`; custom consumers that inspect validation rule codes should switch collection exact-size handling from `size_items` to `size` with `kind: "array"`.
- Manual TypeScript validation schemas now include `TsValidationRule::contains_all(...)` and `TsValidationRule::doesnt_contain_any(...)` helpers for collection membership rules, emitting the canonical `contains` / `doesnt_contain` metadata shape with deduplicated `values` and matching `value` summary params.
- Manual TypeScript validation schemas now include helpers for sibling-field rule metadata, including conditional value rules (`required_if`, `accepted_if`, etc.), sibling presence rules (`required_with`, `prohibited_if_accepted`, etc.), and cross-field comparison rules (`confirmed`, `same`, `before_or_equal`, `date_equals`, etc.), so manual validators can emit derive-compatible `other` / `value` params without hand-building them.
- Manual TypeScript validation schemas now include typed helpers for scalar, numeric, format, list, collection-size, and file-size rule metadata, such as `TsValidationRule::min(8)`, `decimal(2, 4)`, `starts_with([...])`, `in_list([...])`, `uuid_version(4)`, and `max_file_size(2048)`, reducing hand-written `param("...")` keys in manual validators.
- Manual TypeScript validation schemas now include server-only helpers for backend-owned checks such as `unique`, `exists`, schema-level `after` hooks, image validation, MIME sniffing, and image dimensions. These constructors emit the same metadata shape as derive-generated validation while marking rules server-only by default.
- Derived OpenAPI DTO schemas now render `Vec<T>` fields through the same array `ApiSchema` contract used by route roots, including the `x-foundry-item-schema` marker. JSON output is unchanged. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate OpenAPI docs/clients if custom tooling reads Foundry's item-schema marker from DTO properties.
- `Timezone` now exports as a first-class Foundry string scalar for generated TypeScript route helpers and OpenAPI schemas, matching its existing string JSON representation and validation rule support. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/OpenAPI docs if routes or DTOs use `foundry::support::Timezone` directly.
- Backend and generated TypeScript `url` validation now reject literal whitespace before URL parser normalization, so values such as ` https://example.com ` or `https://example.com/path with space` fail while percent-encoded URLs such as `https://example.com/path%20with%20space` remain valid. **Consumer follow-up:** encode spaces in URL fields and regenerate frontend types so client-side validation matches the stricter backend rule.
- Generated TypeScript `timezone` validation now embeds Foundry's backend `chrono_tz` timezone table instead of using browser `Intl` acceptance, so browser-only aliases such as `PST` or lower-case IANA names like `asia/kuala_lumpur` fail before submit just like the Rust validator. `UTC` and fixed offsets such as `+08:00` / `+0800` remain valid. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types and replace browser-only timezone aliases with exact backend timezone names or fixed offsets.
- Generated TypeScript validation metadata now marks `#[validate(json)]` on `serde_json::Value` and nullable JSON value fields as server-only, preventing client-side rejection of valid object/array/scalar JSON payloads while preserving JSON text prevalidation for string fields. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types and remove local JSON stringification/cast workarounds around generated route helpers.
- Generated TypeScript now exports `serde_json::Value` fields and route schemas through a generated recursive `JsonValue` union instead of falling back to `unknown`, and tracks `serde_json/JsonValue.ts` in Foundry's generated types manifest. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; code that used broad `unknown` casts for JSON payloads can switch to `JsonValue` and narrow object properties before access.
- Framework-owned generated TypeScript DTOs now use the shared `JsonValue` contract for JSON payload fields, including `Actor.claims`, WebSocket payloads, `WebSocketHistoryMessageResponse.payload`, `AuditLog` snapshots, `Attachment.custom_properties`, `ModelMeta.value`, `Setting.value` / `parameters`, `NotificationBroadcastPayload.data`, and datatable row values. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; update hand-written mocks/interfaces and broad `unknown` casts to import `JsonValue`, then narrow object properties before access.
- `types:export` now fails route helper generation when a documented request or response schema is not registered for TypeScript export, instead of silently generating `unknown` request/response aliases. **Consumer follow-up:** derive `foundry::ts_rs::TS` alongside `foundry::ApiSchema`, register a manual `foundry::TS` export, or mark intentionally server-only routes with `client_export(false)` / `without_client_export()`.
- Client-exported route helpers now require at least one documented `2xx` response instead of generating `unknown` response aliases for request-only or error-only routes. **Consumer follow-up:** add a success response such as `response::<()>(204)` or `response::<YourDto>(200)` to frontend-callable routes, or mark routes that should not generate helpers with `client_export(false)` / `without_client_export()`.
- Route manifest collection and fallible OpenAPI generation now reject manual container-like `ApiSchema` route roots that omit Foundry's inner schema metadata instead of emitting `Array<unknown>`, `Map<unknown>`, or wrapper aliases with unknown item types. **Consumer follow-up:** update hand-written array/map/wrapper `ApiSchema::schema()` implementations to include `x-foundry-item-schema`, `x-foundry-additional-schema`, or `x-foundry-data-schema`, or use Foundry's built-in `Vec<T>`, set, string-keyed map, `Collection<T>`, `PaginatedResponse<T>`, and `CursorPaginated<T>` schema implementations.
- Backend `email` validation now matches generated TypeScript by requiring bracketed IP-literal domains to occupy the whole domain, so malformed values such as `user@prefix[127.0.0.1]` are rejected while `user@[127.0.0.1]`, single-label domains, and IDN domains remain valid. **Consumer follow-up:** remove any reliance on prefixed IP-literal email domains; regenerate frontend types so client-side validation copy and backend behavior stay aligned.
- Generated TypeScript `validateForm()` now embeds the backend app timezone and uses it for offset-less `datetime`, `before`, `after`, and `date_equals` comparisons, matching Rust's `DateTime::parse_in_timezone` behavior instead of the browser's local timezone. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; forms that compared offset-less datetimes in the user's browser timezone should now expect backend-timezone results.
- Generated TypeScript `validateForm()` now mirrors Rust chrono parsing for expanded date years: unsigned years must stay four digits, while expanded years require an explicit sign such as `+10000-01-01`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; forms that previously accepted unsigned expanded years like `10000-01-01` will now show the same client-side date error the backend would return.
- Generated TypeScript `validateForm()` now treats nullable collection fields like backend `Option<Vec<T>>`: absent/null values skip validation, while present empty arrays still run collection rules such as `min_items`, `size`, `contains`, and file item checks. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; optional array inputs that submit `[]` may now show client-side collection errors that previously appeared only after the backend response.
- `#[derive(Validate)]` now treats `#[serde(skip)]` and `#[serde(skip_deserializing)]` fields as skipped request fields for generated multipart extraction and strict TypeScript validation metadata, and rejects field-level `#[validate(...)]` rules on those skipped inputs. Generated multipart extraction ignores submitted skipped fields and initializes them from field/struct defaults or `Default::default()`, matching serde deserialization more closely. **Consumer follow-up:** stop sending skipped fields through multipart forms, remove validation rules from skipped request fields or remove the serde skip, and regenerate frontend types when strict `knownFields` metadata is used.
- `#[derive(Validate)]` now rejects struct-level custom message/attribute metadata that cannot be tied to request validation metadata: `messages(...)` and `attributes(...)` must target fields with validation rules or fields on a DTO with an `after(...)` hook, and message rule names must match a reachable field rule unless `after(...)` can emit server-only rule codes. Generated TypeScript validation metadata now exports `knownFields` for after-hook DTOs so hook-only field messages remain verifiable without enabling unknown-field rejection. **Consumer follow-up:** fix typos in `messages(field(rule = "..."))` / `attributes(field = "...")`, move custom copy to a field that actually validates, add the matching field-level rule, or keep custom after-hook rule messages on a real request field before regenerating frontend types.
