- `#[derive(Validate)]` now accepts `min_length(...)` and `max_length(...)` as aliases for `min(...)` and `max(...)`, matching `#[derive(ApiSchema)]`; backend errors, generated TypeScript validation metadata, and struct-level custom messages still use canonical `min` / `max` rule codes, with `messages(field(min_length = "..."))` / `messages(field(max_length = "..."))` normalized. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types if you previously used `min_length` / `max_length` only on `ApiSchema` DTOs and expected matching frontend validation.
- Foundry contract derives now reject TypeScript-only wire renames via `#[ts(rename = "...")]` or `#[ts(rename_all = "...")]` on public contracts, covering `#[derive(Validate)]`, `#[derive(ApiSchema)]`, and `#[derive(foundry::TS)]`. Serde remains the single source of truth for JSON/OpenAPI/validation/TypeScript property names. **Consumer follow-up:** replace public `ts(rename)` / `ts(rename_all)` usage with `#[serde(rename = "...")]` or `#[serde(rename_all = "...")]`, then regenerate frontend types and OpenAPI docs.
- Derived OpenAPI schemas now fail fast when `#[serde(flatten)]` expands duplicate property names from parent fields or multiple flattened children instead of silently overwriting one schema entry. **Consumer follow-up:** give every flattened public property a unique serde wire name, move conflicting fields out of flattening, or split the DTO before regenerating OpenAPI docs/frontend types.
- Foundry contract derives now reject public DTO fields and plain contract enum variants that resolve to the same serde JSON name, public aliases via `#[serde(alias = "...")]`, and custom public field codecs such as `#[serde(with = "...")]`, `#[serde(serialize_with = "...")]`, or `#[serde(deserialize_with = "...")]`, covering `#[derive(Validate)]`, `#[derive(ApiSchema)]`, and `#[derive(foundry::TS)]`. This prevents OpenAPI property maps/enum values, generated TypeScript fields/unions, and validation metadata from silently disagreeing about duplicate keys, hidden aliases, variant values, or hidden wire transforms. **Consumer follow-up:** give each public DTO field or enum variant a unique `#[serde(rename = "...")]` / `rename_all` result, remove aliases and custom serde codecs from public contracts, mark truly internal fields with `#[serde(skip)]` / `#[ts(skip)]`, normalize legacy input before it enters a typed DTO, or split ambiguous/legacy request DTOs and enums.
- Derived OpenAPI schemas now expose `#[validate(nullable)]` and `#[validate(bail)]` as `x-foundry-validation` metadata, reject unknown field-level or struct-level `#[validate(...)]` names, validate struct-level `messages(...)` / `attributes(...)` syntax, reject blank or duplicate validation messages/attributes, reject positional arguments on no-argument rules, reject extra positional values on single-argument rules, reject malformed file/AppEnum rule arity, and reject empty `each()` rules instead of silently ignoring malformed metadata. **Consumer follow-up:** fix misspelled or unsupported validation attributes on DTOs that derive `ApiSchema`, including typoed schema hooks such as `after(...)`, correct malformed custom message/attribute metadata, remove blank or repeated `message = "..."` / `messages(...)` / `attributes(...)` entries, write per-rule copy as `required(message = "...")` rather than `required("...")`, remove extra values such as `min(3, 5)` or `max_file_size(1024, 2048)`, and replace `each()` with at least one nested item rule; keep `nullable` as validation metadata rather than relying on it to make a non-`Option` Rust field accept JSON `null`.
- Generated TypeScript `validateForm()` now translates common Rust regex syntax before client-side `regex` / `not_regex` checks, including leading `(?i)`, `(?m)`, `(?s)` flags and `(?P<name>...)` captures; Rust-only patterns are represented as server-only validation metadata. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; forms may now show client-side regex errors for backend patterns that were previously skipped in the browser.
- Generated TypeScript and OpenAPI schemas now expose queued datatable export responses as `DatatableExportAccepted` with a backend-owned `DatatableExportStatus` enum instead of a loose `string`; the JSON status value remains `"queued"`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types/OpenAPI clients and replace hand-written datatable export accepted interfaces or status unions with the generated contracts.
- Generated TypeScript route helpers now understand documented `PaginatedResponse<T>` and `CursorPaginated<T>` responses, rendering concrete `{ data, meta, links }` / `{ data, meta, cursors }` aliases with backend-owned pagination metadata imports instead of falling back to `unknown`. `CursorMeta` and `CursorInfo` are exported alongside the existing offset pagination contracts. Existing JSON output is unchanged. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types and replace hand-written paginated response or cursor metadata interfaces with the generated route response aliases, `PaginationMeta` / `PaginationLinks`, and `CursorMeta` / `CursorInfo`.
- Generated TypeScript now exports job observability response contracts (`JobsStatsResponse`, `JobStatusCountResponse`, `JobsFailedResponse`, and `FailedJobResponse`), and their `status` fields now import the backend-owned `JobHistoryStatus` enum instead of widening to `string`. The HTTP JSON values remain unchanged. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types and replace hand-written `/_foundry/jobs/stats` / `/_foundry/jobs/failed` interfaces or status unions with the generated job observability contracts.
- Generated TypeScript now exports the framework-owned WebSocket protocol records `ClientMessage`, `ServerMessage`, `PresenceInfo`, and `WebSocketChannelDescriptor`, including `JsonValue` payload fields and optional sparse frame properties. The channel-aware `WebSocketChannelManifest` helpers remain available as the ergonomic frontend layer. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types and replace hand-written raw WebSocket frame, presence member, or channel descriptor interfaces with the generated records where custom socket clients or dashboards need the backend wire shape.
- Generated `WebSocketChannelManifest.ts` frame aliases and builders now default app message/client-event payload generics to the backend-owned `JsonValue` contract, and inbound frame guards reject non-JSON payload values before narrowing app frames. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; convert `Date`, `File`, `Map`, class instances, or other non-JSON browser objects to JSON-friendly DTOs before passing them to `messageToChannel()` / `clientEventToChannel()`, or before expecting `parseWebSocketServerFrame()` to accept manually constructed frames.
- Generated TypeScript now exports the WebSocket `ClientAction` protocol enum with AppEnum-style values, metadata, key constants, and guards, while `WebSocketClientAction` aliases that backend-owned enum instead of duplicating the action union in `WebSocketChannelManifest.ts`. Existing snake_case wire output and PascalCase input compatibility are preserved. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types and replace hand-written WebSocket action unions with `ClientAction`, `ClientActionKeys`, or the existing `WebSocketClientAction` alias.
- Generated TypeScript now exports logging and runtime diagnostic enums (`LogLevel`, `HttpOutcomeClass`, `AuthOutcome`, `JobOutcome`, `WebSocketConnectionState`, `RuntimeBackendKind`, `SchedulerLeadershipState`, and `ProbeState`) with AppEnum-style values, metadata, key constants, and guards. Health/readiness/runtime response DTOs now import those backend-owned enum contracts instead of leaving clients to duplicate string unions. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types and replace hand-written observability / health-state unions with the generated enum helpers.
- Generated TypeScript now exports `AuthErrorCode` with AppEnum-style values, options, metadata, key constants, and runtime guards for Foundry's built-in auth `error_code` strings. `ErrorResponse.error_code` remains `string` so app-specific codes still fit the generic error envelope. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types and replace hand-written auth error-code unions or string-literal checks with `AuthErrorCode`, `AuthErrorCodeKeys`, and `isAuthErrorCode()` where appropriate.
- Generated TypeScript now exports the framework-owned `Actor` auth identity shape, and OpenAPI schema generation now treats `BTreeSet<T>` as an array so role/permission sets can be documented. `roles`, `permissions`, and `claims` are optional in the generated type to match existing Actor deserialization compatibility. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types and replace hand-written `/me` or auth-state actor interfaces with the generated `Actor`.
- Generated TypeScript now exports the built-in `AuditLog` model used by audit review/admin screens, including nullable JSON snapshot fields as `JsonValue | null`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types and replace hand-written audit log row interfaces with the generated `AuditLog`, narrowing `before_data`, `after_data`, and `changes` per audited model where needed.
- Generated TypeScript now exports model-extension metadata and translation records: `ModelMeta`, `ModelTranslation`, and `TranslatedFields`. `ModelMeta.value` is generated as `JsonValue | null` so app-specific metadata stays explicit at the edge. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types and replace hand-written model metadata / translated-field interfaces with the generated records.
- Generated TypeScript now exports framework-owned MFA request and response DTOs: `MfaCodeRequest`, `MfaEnrollChallenge`, `MfaRecoveryCodesRequest`, and `MfaRecoveryCodesResponse`. Existing Rust `foundry::auth::mfa::CodeRequest` / `EnrollChallenge` / `RecoveryCodesRequest` / `RecoveryCodesResponse` names remain available as aliases. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types and replace hand-written MFA setup, verification, disable, and recovery-code interfaces with the generated types.
- `Attachment` records are now serde-serializable and exported by generated TypeScript, including storage metadata and `custom_properties: JsonValue` for app-specific narrowing. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types and replace hand-written attachment interfaces or API resource DTOs with the generated `Attachment` where endpoints return Foundry attachment records directly.
- Generated TypeScript now exports the framework-owned `StoredFile` and `StorageObject` storage response records, keeping upload/write results and prefix-listing metadata backend-owned. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types and replace hand-written upload result or storage-browser interfaces with the generated types.
- Generated TypeScript now exports the framework-owned `Setting` record next to `SettingType`, including setting values and admin form metadata from the backend settings store. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types and replace hand-written setting record interfaces with the generated `Setting` type, narrowing `value` / `parameters` from `JsonValue` in app-specific code.
- Built-in broadcast notifications now publish a typed `NotificationBroadcastPayload` envelope as WebSocket payload: `{ notification_type, data }`. The `notification_type` comes from `Notification::notification_type()` and `data` is the JSON returned by `Notification::to_broadcast()`, so frontend clients can dispatch notification broadcasts from backend-owned metadata instead of requiring every notification payload to duplicate its own type field. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types and update WebSocket notification handlers from reading raw payload fields such as `payload.message` to reading `payload.data.message`; dispatch by `payload.notification_type` instead of custom per-notification `type` fields.
- Generated TypeScript AppEnum exports now include runtime helpers `get{Name}Values()`, `get{Name}Options()`, `get{Name}Meta()`, `is{Name}()`, `get{Name}Option()`, and `get{Name}LabelKey()` next to `Values`, `Options`, and `Meta`, plus `get{Name}Keys()` / `get{Name}Groups()` when key/group constants are generated, so frontends can validate unknown values and resolve or safely copy backend-owned enum metadata instead of duplicating enum lookup logic. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types and replace hand-written enum guards / option lookups with the generated helpers where possible.
- Generated TypeScript datatable query helpers now serialize exact-match filters with an explicit `f-eq-<field>` query key, and backend `DatatableRequest` query parsing accepts that key while keeping the older `f-<field>` exact-match fallback. This removes ambiguity for exact filters whose backend-owned field name starts with an operator prefix such as `in-`, `date-`, or `not-eq-`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; custom raw datatable query builders should emit `f-eq-<field>` for exact filters. If a legacy client intentionally sent `f-eq-status` to mean exact field `eq-status`, send `f-eq-eq-status` after this change.
- Direct TypeScript datatable manifest export now rejects descriptor metadata that would make generated table helpers ambiguous: blank or whitespace-padded field names, duplicate column/mapping/default-sort names, and static filter field collisions between filterable columns and relation filter fields or aliases. **Consumer follow-up:** for hand-built `DatatableDescriptor` values, keep frontend-visible names trimmed and unique, or prefer registry-collected descriptors.
- Generated TypeScript WebSocket protocol frame types and `isWebSocketProtocolFrame()` now derive presence-channel eligibility from the backend channel manifest, so `presence:join` / `presence:leave` are treated as Foundry protocol frames only for channels registered with `presence(true)`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; code that handled `WebSocketPresenceJoinFrame<SomeNonPresenceChannel>` should narrow on `isWebSocketPresenceChannelName(channel)` or treat app-published events with those names as ordinary server events instead of Foundry presence protocol frames.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint helpers now encode GET/HEAD query-transport DTOs through Foundry's own route query encoder instead of passing raw DTO arrays to the HTTP adapter's `params` serializer, and OpenAPI query array parameters now explicitly use `style: form` + `explode: true` to document the same repeated-key shape. Arrays now use repeated keys like `tag=rust&tag=dx`, `null` / `undefined` query values are skipped, and explicit query-transport overrides with nested object fields fail fast because Foundry's typed route query contract only supports scalar values and scalar arrays. **Consumer follow-up:** after regenerating frontend types/OpenAPI clients, custom HTTP clients or request interceptors that inspected generated query DTOs via `config.params` should read the already-encoded `config.url` instead; flatten nested query fields into scalar DTO fields before using GET/HEAD typed route helpers.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint helpers now report client-side validation errors for root container request schemas with the container path before the DTO field, such as `[0].email` and `[tenant].email`, instead of field-first keys like `email[0]`. This matches the readable parent-prefix style used by nested backend validation paths. **Consumer follow-up:** if frontend code reads client-side errors for `Array<Dto>` or `Map<Dto>` request helpers by the old field-first keys, switch to the new container-prefixed keys after regenerating types.
- `#[derive(Validate)]` now validates `Vec<UploadedFile>` and `Option<Vec<UploadedFile>>` as first-class multi-file upload fields: collection count rules stay on the base field, file rules run against each uploaded file with indexed error paths, and absent optional multi-file fields skip file checks unless a presence rule requires them. Generated TypeScript route helpers expose the same collection and file metadata for upload forms, prevalidate browser-checkable file rules per indexed file, and generated OpenAPI schemas place file-count constraints on the array while keeping per-file upload metadata on the array `items` schema. **Consumer follow-up:** multi-file upload DTOs can move per-file size/extension rules and file-count rules onto the field attribute, then regenerate frontend types/OpenAPI docs.
- Derived multipart extraction now honors `#[serde(default)]` and `#[serde(default = "...")]` for absent fields, matching JSON request deserialization instead of treating defaulted non-`Option` fields as missing required multipart parts. Present multipart values still parse and validate normally, and invalid present values still fail with `400 Bad Request`. **Consumer follow-up:** if a form intentionally omits defaulted DTO fields, remove local multipart workarounds and keep the default on the DTO as the SSOT.
- `#[derive(Validate)]` now treats `Option<Vec<T>>` as a first-class collection for `min_items`, `max_items`, `size`, `distinct`, `contains`, `doesnt_contain`, `each(...)`, and `each(nested)`. Absent optional collections skip collection and item rules unless a presence rule requires them, generated TypeScript route helpers emit the same derived `nullable` collection metadata, and multipart extraction can build optional repeated fields from repeated form parts. **Consumer follow-up:** optional-array request DTOs can now move validation rules from custom hooks onto the field attribute and regenerate frontend types/OpenAPI docs.
- `#[derive(Validate)]` now supports explicit nested DTO validation through `#[validate(nested)]` on child DTO fields and `#[validate(each(nested))]` on `Vec<ChildDto>` fields. Backend errors are prefixed with the parent path, generated TypeScript route helpers embed the child validation schema for client prevalidation, and derived OpenAPI schemas expose the same nested rule through `x-foundry-validation`. Existing DTO-shaped fields are not validated recursively unless they opt in. **Consumer follow-up:** add `nested` / `each(nested)` where child DTOs should be validated, then regenerate frontend types and OpenAPI clients/docs.
- `#[derive(Validate)]` now reports validation error fields, struct-level custom messages/attributes, generated TypeScript validation metadata, and generated multipart field matching with serde wire names from `rename` / `rename_all`, matching derived TypeScript DTO property names and OpenAPI schemas. Validation attribute references such as `required_if("other_field", ...)` still use Rust field identifiers so the macro can type-check sibling access. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; any frontend or backend code that matches derived validation errors for serde-renamed DTOs by Rust names like `audit_note` should switch to the wire name like `auditNote`.
- Derived OpenAPI schemas now expose validation-only rules such as `required_if`, `required_with_all`, `confirmed`, `same`, temporal comparisons, `prohibits`, `unique`, and `exists` through an `x-foundry-validation` vendor extension that mirrors generated TypeScript route-helper metadata (`code`, `params`, `values`, `serverOnly`). Field references in this OpenAPI metadata use the same serde wire names as schema properties. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate OpenAPI clients/docs after adding these validation rules so docs and custom tooling can read the backend-owned validation contract instead of rediscovering it locally.
- Derived OpenAPI schemas now expose field-local `#[validate(numeric)]`, `#[validate(integer)]`, `#[validate(ip)]`, `#[validate(json)]`, `#[validate(lowercase)]`, and `#[validate(uppercase)]` constraints where they can be represented without changing the field wire type. Generated TypeScript endpoint helpers also include backend-matched fallback messages for server-only upload validation codes. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate OpenAPI clients/docs and frontend types after adding these validation rules so schema tooling and client-side fallback copy match the backend contract.
- Derived OpenAPI schemas now expose upload validation metadata for `#[validate(max_file_size(...))]`, `#[validate(allowed_extensions(...))]`, `#[validate(image)]`, `#[validate(allowed_mimes(...))]`, `#[validate(max_dimensions(...))]`, and `#[validate(min_dimensions(...))]` through `x-foundry-*` vendor extensions, matching the backend validator and generated TypeScript route-helper metadata. Content-sniffing rules are also listed in `x-foundry-server-only-validation`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate OpenAPI clients/docs after adding these file validation rules so upload forms and generated client tooling can see the backend-owned file contract.
- Derived OpenAPI schemas now expose `#[validate(timezone)]` string fields with a custom `format: "timezone"` marker, matching the backend validator and generated TypeScript prevalidation metadata. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate OpenAPI clients/docs after adding `#[validate(timezone)]` so schema tooling can see the timezone contract.
- `#[derive(Validate)]` now supports Laravel-style `#[validate(confirmed)]`, defaulting to the sibling `<field>_confirmation` while keeping `confirmed("field")` for custom confirmation fields. The macro checks the default sibling at compile time and generated TypeScript validation metadata still emits the resolved `other` field. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types after switching DTOs from `confirmed("password_confirmation")` to `confirmed` so comments and client prevalidation stay in sync.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint helpers now use the same fallback message as the Rust validator for `timezone` prevalidation failures instead of falling back to a generic invalid-field message. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types after using `#[validate(timezone)]` so client-side validation displays the backend-owned timezone message.
- Validation now supports Laravel-style exact `size` semantics through `.size(n)` for strings, `.size_numeric(n)` for numbers, `.size_items(n)` for collections, and type-aware `#[validate(size(n))]` on DTO fields. Derived validators route Rust string, numeric, and `Vec<T>` fields to the correct backend rule, generated TypeScript endpoint helpers prevalidate the same `size` metadata, and derived OpenAPI schemas emit exact length, value, or item-count constraints. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types and OpenAPI clients/docs after adding `#[validate(size(...))]` to DTOs so client-side validation and schema tooling include the exact-size contract.
- Validation now supports Laravel-style array containment rules through `.contains_all([...])`, `.doesnt_contain_any([...])`, and `#[validate(contains("a", "b"))]` / `#[validate(doesnt_contain("a", "b"))]` on `Vec<T>` fields. The existing string substring `contains("needle")` path remains available for scalar fields and `each(contains(...))`, while vector fields now emit backend-owned TypeScript `values` metadata and OpenAPI `contains` / `not.contains` constraints. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types and OpenAPI clients/docs after adding vector containment validation so client-side validation and schema tooling include the new array constraints.
- Validation prefix/suffix rules now accept Laravel-style multiple allowed or forbidden values: `.starts_with_any([...])`, `.doesnt_start_with_any([...])`, `.ends_with_any([...])`, `.doesnt_end_with_any([...])`, and `#[validate(starts_with("a", "b"))]` / `#[validate(doesnt_end_with("a", "b"))]`. Single-value builder methods and attributes remain supported; runtime messages join the configured values, generated TypeScript endpoint helpers prevalidate from backend-owned `values` metadata, and derived OpenAPI schemas emit `anyOf` / `not.anyOf` pattern constraints where needed. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types and OpenAPI clients/docs after adding multi-value prefix/suffix validation so client-side validation and schema tooling include the expanded constraints.
- Validation now supports Laravel-style version-constrained UUID checks through `.uuid_version(version)` and `#[validate(uuid(version))]`, while preserving the existing `.uuid()` / `#[validate(uuid)]` shape. Runtime validation checks the parsed UUID version nibble across canonical, compact, braced, and `urn:uuid:` forms; generated TypeScript endpoint helpers prevalidate the same optional `version` metadata, and derived OpenAPI schemas retain `format: uuid` with a compatible version pattern when representable. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types and OpenAPI clients/docs after adding version-constrained UUID validation to DTOs so generated clients include the stricter rule metadata.
- Validation now includes Laravel-style temporal equality through `.date_equals(field, value)` and `#[validate(date_equals("field"))]`. Runtime validation reuses Foundry's normalized temporal comparison across `DateTime`, `LocalDateTime`, `Date`, and `Time` strings, derived validators validate referenced sibling fields at compile time, and generated TypeScript endpoint helpers prevalidate the same temporal equality from backend-owned DTO metadata. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types after adding this rule to DTOs so client-side validation metadata includes the new date-equality check.
- Validation now includes Laravel-style strict numeric comparison rules through `.gt(value)`, `.gte(value)`, `.lt(value)`, `.lte(value)`, and matching `#[validate(...)]` attributes. Runtime validation rejects non-finite/non-numeric input, generated TypeScript endpoint helpers prevalidate the same parsed numeric comparisons, and derived OpenAPI schemas emit `exclusiveMinimum` / `minimum` / `exclusiveMaximum` / `maximum` constraints where representable. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types and OpenAPI clients/docs after adding these rules to DTOs so client-side validation and schema tooling include the new numeric bounds.
- Validation now includes Laravel-style prohibited presence rules through `.prohibited()`, `.prohibited_if(field, value, expected)`, `.prohibited_unless(field, value, except)`, `.prohibited_if_accepted(field, value)`, `.prohibited_if_declined(field, value)`, and matching `#[validate(...)]` attributes. Derived validators validate referenced sibling fields at compile time, generated TypeScript endpoint helpers prevalidate the same forbidden-field conditions, and optional prohibited fields keep auto-nullable behavior so absent values remain allowed. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types after adding these rules to DTOs so client-side validation metadata includes the new prohibited checks.
- Validation now includes Laravel-style `prohibits` checks through `.prohibits([(field, value), ...])` and `#[validate(prohibits("field", ...))]`. Runtime validation rejects listed sibling fields when the current value is present, derived validators validate referenced sibling fields at compile time, and generated TypeScript endpoint helpers prevalidate the same mutually-exclusive field set from backend-owned metadata. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types after adding this rule to DTOs so client-side validation metadata includes the new sibling prohibition contract.
- Validation now includes Laravel-style consent-aware presence rules through `.required_if_accepted(field, value)` / `.required_if_declined(field, value)` and `#[validate(required_if_accepted("field"))]` / `#[validate(required_if_declined("field"))]`. Derived validators validate referenced sibling fields at compile time, avoid auto-nullable skipping on `Option<T>` targets, and generated TypeScript endpoint helpers prevalidate the same accepted/declined sibling conditions. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types after adding these rules to DTOs so client-side validation metadata includes the new conditional required checks.
- Validation now includes Laravel-style `filled` presence validation through `.filled()` and `#[validate(filled)]`, including non-empty `Vec<T>` checks in derived validators. Derived validators no longer auto-nullable-skip `Option<T>` fields carrying `filled`, derived OpenAPI schemas expose non-empty string/array constraints where representable, and generated TypeScript endpoint helpers prevalidate the same non-empty rule from backend-owned DTO metadata. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types and OpenAPI clients/docs after adding `#[validate(filled)]` to DTOs; optional fields with `filled` now reject `None` / `null` / empty strings instead of being treated as nullable.
- Validation now includes a Laravel-style `boolean` rule through `.boolean()` and `#[validate(boolean)]`, accepting `true`, `false`, `1`, and `0`. Derived OpenAPI schemas document string-backed boolean fields with the accepted enum values, and generated TypeScript endpoint helpers prevalidate the same rule. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types after adding `#[validate(boolean)]` to DTOs so client-side validation metadata includes the new rule.
- Validation now includes Laravel-style `accepted` and `declined` rules through `.accepted()` / `.declined()` and `#[validate(accepted)]` / `#[validate(declined)]`. OpenAPI schemas document accepted string/boolean values, and generated TypeScript endpoint helpers prevalidate the same consent/opt-out rules. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types after adding these rules to DTOs so client-side validation metadata includes them.
- Validation now includes Laravel-style conditional consent rules through `.accepted_if(field, value, expected)` / `.declined_if(field, value, expected)` and `#[validate(accepted_if("field", "expected"))]` / `#[validate(declined_if("field", "expected"))]`. Derived validators validate referenced sibling fields at compile time, generated TypeScript endpoint helpers prevalidate the same sibling-field conditions, and OpenAPI derive treats them as validation metadata rather than unconditional enum constraints. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types after adding these rules to DTOs so client-side validation metadata includes the new conditional checks.
- Validation now includes a `contains` string rule through `.contains("needle")` and `#[validate(contains("needle"))]`. Derived OpenAPI schemas expose it as an escaped literal `pattern`, and generated TypeScript endpoint helpers prevalidate the same substring check. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types after adding `#[validate(contains(...))]` to DTOs so client-side validation metadata includes the new rule.
- Validation now includes a scalar `doesnt_contain` string rule through `.doesnt_contain("needle")` and `#[validate(doesnt_contain("needle"))]` on non-collection DTO fields. The existing `Vec<T>` membership form still maps to `.doesnt_contain_any([...])`; scalar OpenAPI schemas now emit a negative substring pattern and generated TypeScript endpoint helpers prevalidate the same backend-owned metadata. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types and OpenAPI clients/docs after adding scalar `#[validate(doesnt_contain(...))]` to DTOs so client-side validation and schema tooling include the new negative substring contract.
- Validation now includes Laravel-style negative prefix/suffix string rules through `.doesnt_start_with(prefix)` / `.doesnt_end_with(suffix)` and `#[validate(doesnt_start_with(...))]` / `#[validate(doesnt_end_with(...))]`. Derived OpenAPI schemas emit escaped `not.pattern` constraints, and generated TypeScript endpoint helpers prevalidate the same forbidden prefix/suffix checks from backend-owned DTO metadata. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types and OpenAPI clients/docs after adding these rules to DTOs so client-side validation and schema tooling include the new constraints.
- Validation now includes Laravel-style alpha-dash validation through `.alpha_dash()` and `#[validate(alpha_dash)]`, accepting Unicode letters, marks, numbers, plus ASCII dashes and underscores. Derived OpenAPI schemas expose the same accepted shape as a JSON Schema `pattern`, and generated TypeScript endpoint helpers prevalidate the rule from backend-owned DTO metadata. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types and OpenAPI clients/docs after adding `#[validate(alpha_dash)]` to DTOs so client-side validation and schema tooling include the new rule.
- Validation `alpha` and `alpha_numeric` now match Laravel's Unicode mark handling, accepting combining marks alongside letters / alpha-numeric characters, and Laravel's `alpha_num` spelling is available through `.alpha_num()` and `#[validate(alpha_num)]`. Derived OpenAPI schemas now expose `alpha`, `alpha_num`, and `alpha_numeric` as JSON Schema patterns, and generated TypeScript endpoint helpers prevalidate both alpha-numeric spellings. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types and OpenAPI clients/docs; existing `alpha` / `alpha_numeric` fields may now accept composed Unicode names that previously failed, while schema tooling may begin enforcing the documented patterns.
- Validation now includes Laravel-style ASCII validation through `.ascii()` and `#[validate(ascii)]`. Derived OpenAPI schemas expose it as a JSON Schema `pattern`, and generated TypeScript endpoint helpers prevalidate the same ASCII-only check from backend-owned DTO metadata. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types and OpenAPI clients/docs after adding `#[validate(ascii)]` to DTOs so client-side validation and schema tooling include the new rule.
- Validation now includes Laravel-style ULID validation through `.ulid()` and `#[validate(ulid)]`. Derived OpenAPI schemas expose the ULID alphabet/length as a JSON Schema `pattern`, and generated TypeScript endpoint helpers prevalidate the same rule from backend-owned DTO metadata. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types and OpenAPI clients/docs after adding `#[validate(ulid)]` to DTOs so client-side validation and schema tooling include the new rule.
- Validation now includes Laravel-style hex color validation through `.hex_color()` and `#[validate(hex_color)]`, accepting `#RGB`, `#RGBA`, `#RRGGBB`, and `#RRGGBBAA` forms. Derived OpenAPI schemas expose the same accepted forms as a JSON Schema `pattern`, and generated TypeScript endpoint helpers prevalidate the same rule from backend-owned DTO metadata. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types and OpenAPI clients/docs after adding `#[validate(hex_color)]` to DTOs so client-side validation and schema tooling include the new rule.
- Validation now includes Laravel-style MAC address validation through `.mac_address()` and `#[validate(mac_address)]`, accepting six hexadecimal octets separated consistently by `:` or `-`. Derived OpenAPI schemas expose the same accepted forms as a JSON Schema `pattern`, and generated TypeScript endpoint helpers prevalidate the same rule from backend-owned DTO metadata. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types and OpenAPI clients/docs after adding `#[validate(mac_address)]` to DTOs so client-side validation and schema tooling include the new rule.
- Validation now includes Laravel-style decimal-place validation through `.decimal(min, max)` and `#[validate(decimal(min))]` / `#[validate(decimal(min, max))]`. Runtime validation, derived TypeScript endpoint helpers, and derived OpenAPI schemas now share the same textual precision checks. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types and OpenAPI clients/docs after adding `#[validate(decimal(...))]` to DTOs; prefer `String` or exact decimal-text request fields when the number of decimal places matters because binary floating-point fields cannot preserve trailing zeros.
- Validation now includes Laravel-style multiple validation through `.multiple_of(value)` and `#[validate(multiple_of(value))]`. Derived OpenAPI schemas emit `multipleOf`, and generated TypeScript endpoint helpers prevalidate the same finite numeric multiple check from backend-owned DTO metadata. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types and OpenAPI clients/docs after adding `#[validate(multiple_of(...))]` to DTOs so client-side validation and schema tooling include the new rule.
- Validation now includes Laravel-style digit length rules through `.min_digits(n)`, `.max_digits(n)`, `.digits_between(min, max)`, and matching `#[validate(...)]` attributes. Derived OpenAPI schemas emit a digit `pattern` plus `minLength` / `maxLength`, and generated TypeScript endpoint helpers prevalidate the same digit-count constraints. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types and OpenAPI clients/docs after adding these rules to DTOs so client-side validation and schema tooling include the new constraints.
- Validation now includes Laravel-style negative regex validation through `.not_regex(pattern)` and `#[validate(not_regex(pattern))]`. Derived OpenAPI schemas emit `not: { pattern: ... }`, and generated TypeScript endpoint helpers prevalidate the same inverse regex check from backend-owned DTO metadata. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types and OpenAPI clients/docs after adding `#[validate(not_regex(...))]` to DTOs so client-side validation and schema tooling include the new rule.
- Validation now includes Laravel-style casing rules through `.lowercase()` / `.uppercase()` and `#[validate(lowercase)]` / `#[validate(uppercase)]`. Generated TypeScript endpoint helpers prevalidate the same casing checks from backend-owned DTO metadata. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types after adding these rules to DTOs so client-side validation metadata includes them.
- Validation now includes collection cardinality rules through `.min_items(n)` / `.max_items(n)` on `Validator::each(...)` and `#[validate(min_items(n), max_items(n))]` on `Vec<T>` DTO fields. Derived OpenAPI schemas emit `minItems` / `maxItems`, and generated TypeScript endpoint helpers prevalidate array length before submit. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types after adding these rules to DTOs so client-side validation metadata includes them.
- Validation now includes Laravel-style collection uniqueness through `.distinct()` on `Validator::each(...)` and `#[validate(distinct)]` on `Vec<T>` DTO fields. Derived OpenAPI schemas emit `uniqueItems: true`, and generated TypeScript endpoint helpers prevalidate duplicate array values. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types after adding `#[validate(distinct)]` to DTOs so client-side validation metadata includes the new rule.
- Validation now includes Laravel-style conditional presence through `.required_if(field, value, expected)` and `#[validate(required_if("field", "expected"))]`. Derived validators no longer auto-nullable-skip `Option<T>` fields carrying `required_if`, and generated TypeScript endpoint helpers prevalidate the same sibling-field condition. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types after adding `#[validate(required_if(...))]` to DTOs so client-side validation metadata includes the new rule.
- Validation now includes Laravel-style inverse conditional presence through `.required_unless(field, value, except)` and `#[validate(required_unless("field", "except"))]`. It shares the `required_if` typed sibling-field path, avoids auto-nullable skipping on `Option<T>`, and generated TypeScript endpoint helpers prevalidate the same condition. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types after adding `#[validate(required_unless(...))]` to DTOs so client-side validation metadata includes the new rule.
- Validation now includes Laravel-style sibling presence through `.required_with(field, value)` and `#[validate(required_with("field"))]`. Derived validators validate referenced sibling fields at compile time, avoid auto-nullable skipping on `Option<T>` targets, and generated TypeScript endpoint helpers prevalidate the same present-field condition. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types after adding `#[validate(required_with(...))]` to DTOs so client-side validation metadata includes the new rule.
- Validation now includes Laravel-style all-sibling presence through `.required_with_all([(field, value), ...])` and `#[validate(required_with_all("a", "b"))]`. Derived validators validate every referenced sibling field at compile time, avoid auto-nullable skipping on `Option<T>` targets, and generated TypeScript endpoint helpers prevalidate the same all-fields-present condition. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types after adding `#[validate(required_with_all(...))]` to DTOs so client-side validation metadata includes the new rule.
- Validation now includes Laravel-style sibling absence through `.required_without(field, value)` and `#[validate(required_without("field"))]`. Derived validators validate referenced sibling fields at compile time, avoid auto-nullable skipping on `Option<T>` targets, and generated TypeScript endpoint helpers prevalidate the same missing-field condition. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types after adding `#[validate(required_without(...))]` to DTOs so client-side validation metadata includes the new rule.
- Validation now includes Laravel-style all-sibling absence through `.required_without_all([(field, value), ...])` and `#[validate(required_without_all("a", "b"))]`. Derived validators validate every referenced sibling field at compile time, avoid auto-nullable skipping on `Option<T>` targets, and generated TypeScript endpoint helpers prevalidate the same no-fields-present condition. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types after adding `#[validate(required_without_all(...))]` to DTOs so client-side validation metadata includes the new rule.
- Named route URL generation in Rust and generated TypeScript now uses matching RFC3986 path-param percent encoding, including `!'()*`, and preserves `/` separators for Axum catch-all `{*path}` parameters while still percent-encoding each path segment; normal `{id}` and `:id` parameters continue encoding `/` as `%2F`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; route params containing `!'()*` will now produce encoded frontend URLs that match backend `RouteRegistry::url`.
- Rust `RouteRegistry::url` / `AppContext::route_url` now append non-path params as percent-encoded query params, and signed route URLs include those extra params in the signed URL before `expires` / `signature`. Generated TypeScript `routeUrl()` / `createRouteUrlBuilder()` now accept `RouteUrlOptions.query` for the same route-owned URL construction path. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; if backend code passed unused params expecting them to be ignored, remove them or expect them in the query string.
- Generated TypeScript named-route URL helpers now export `EmptyRouteParams`, use it for routes without path params, reject accidental param objects for those routes at type-check time, and allow route options as the first argument for no-param routes. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; code that passed arbitrary objects as params to no-param `routeUrl(...)` calls should remove them or pass route options such as `{ basePath }`.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint helpers now expose typed backend error payloads as `endpoint.errorResponse: ErrorResponse | null` while preserving the raw adapter error in `serverError`, and server-error extraction no longer throws when an adapter error lacks `response.data`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; UI code can read `errorResponse.message`, `errorResponse.error_code`, and `errorResponse.message_key` directly instead of re-parsing caught errors.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint helpers now preserve validation `FieldError` details in `endpoint.errorDetails` and `FoundryValidationClientError.errorDetails` instead of exposing only field-to-message arrays. Existing `endpoint.errors` remains the message map. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; frontend validation UI can branch on `errorDetails[field]?.[0]?.code` without parsing translated messages.
- `types:export` now emits `WebSocketChannelManifest.ts` with registered channel ids, presence/replay/client-event settings, guard, permissions, and typed client-frame builders for subscribe/unsubscribe/message/client-event frames. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; custom WebSocket clients can import `WebSocketChannelIds`, `WebSocketChannelManifest`, and frame helpers instead of duplicating backend channel metadata or hand-building protocol JSON.
- `HttpRegistrar` now has top-level named-route helpers for `get`, `head`, `post`, `put`, `patch`, `delete`, and `options`, matching the scoped route API and recording backend method metadata for generated TypeScript endpoint helpers. `RouteDoc` also has `head()` and `options()` builders. **Consumer follow-up:** prefer these method-aware helpers for named routes that should generate frontend endpoint helpers.
- TypeScript route endpoint helper files are now generated only for named routes that document a request or response schema. URL-only named routes remain in `RouteManifest` and `RouteIds` with `clientExport: false`, avoiding misleading helpers that expose `unknown` contracts. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; if frontend code imported an endpoint helper for an undocumented route, add `request::<T>()` / `response::<T>(status)` docs in Rust or switch that usage to `routeUrl(...)`.
- Generated OpenAPI specs now document object-shaped `request::<T>()` DTOs on GET and HEAD routes as query parameters instead of request bodies, matching generated TypeScript endpoint helper submission behavior. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate OpenAPI clients; clients for affected search/filter endpoints may switch from body arguments to query-parameter arguments.
- Generated OpenAPI operations with typed requests now include `x-foundry-request-transport` (`"body"` / `"query"`), using the same backend transport decision as `RouteManifest.requestTransport`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate OpenAPI clients/docs; custom OpenAPI tooling can read this extension instead of inferring request transport from HTTP method or schema shape.
- Generated TypeScript `RouteManifest` entries and endpoint helpers now expose `requestTransport` (`"body"` / `"query"`), and endpoint submission follows that backend-owned transport metadata instead of inferring from the HTTP method alone. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; custom route tooling should read `requestTransport` when deciding whether request data is sent as body or query params.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint helpers now reject non-object request data when query transport is explicitly forced or route metadata is missing, instead of silently dropping scalar roots or reshaping array roots into numeric query keys. Backend-documented GET/HEAD scalar and array requests continue to use body transport. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; callers that override `requestTransport: "query"` should pass object DTO data or move custom scalar query values into `request.params`.
- `types:export` now emits `DatatableManifest.ts` with registered datatable ids, column metadata, computed mappings, relation-filter aliases, backend default sorts, and `DatatableRuntimeManifest` from datatable config page/export caps. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; table builders can import `DatatableManifest`, `DatatableRuntimeManifest`, `DatatableIds`, `datatablePerPageCap()`, `datatableExportRowsCap()`, `datatableManifestEntry()`, `datatableEntries()`, `datatableColumns()`, `datatableSortableColumns()`, `datatableFilterableColumns()`, `datatableMappings()`, `datatableRelationFilters()`, and `isDatatableName()` instead of duplicating datatable metadata or configured limits. Manual `DynDatatable` implementors should override `descriptor()` to expose static metadata; the compatibility default returns the datatable id with empty metadata.
- Generated `DatatableManifest.ts` now exports typed datatable request helpers: `datatableSort()`, `datatableFilter()`, `datatableDefaultSort()`, `datatableRequest()`, `datatableQueryParams()`, `DatatableRequestFor<Name>`, and field-name aliases derived from backend datatable metadata. `DatatableRequest` deserialization now accepts structured JSON and legacy query params directly, and parses `sort` / `direction` plus additional filter prefixes (`not_eq`, `gt`, `lt`, `in`) instead of silently ignoring them. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; prefer these helpers for table request builders and URL query state instead of raw sortable/filterable field strings. If a consumer currently sends `sort` / `direction` query params while expecting them to be ignored, remove them or update the table route to honor the new sorting behavior. Dynamic `available_filters()` controls can continue sending normal `DatatableFilterInput[]`.
- Generated `DatatableRequestFor<Name>` now narrows `filters` to backend-manifest static filter fields, and `datatableRequest()` rejects stale filter fields the same way it already rejects stale sort fields. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; static table request builders should use `datatableFilter()` or manifest-backed filter fields, while dynamic `available_filters()` controls can keep using the raw generated `DatatableRequest` shape when fields are not part of the static manifest.
- Generated TypeScript `RouteManifest` entries and endpoint helpers now expose `requestMediaType` (`"application/json"` / `"multipart/form-data"` / `null`), and endpoint submission defaults multipart requests from backend-owned metadata instead of inspecting only runtime data for file values. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; custom upload/form tooling should read `requestMediaType` when deciding whether to submit JSON or `FormData`.
- Generated TypeScript `RouteManifestResponse` entries now include `hasBody` and `mediaType`, using the same backend-owned no-content/`Unit` response rule and response media type as OpenAPI. Endpoint helper response aliases now use that metadata, so bodyless statuses such as `204` generate `void` even if a non-`Unit` schema was accidentally documented. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; custom route manifest interfaces should add `hasBody` and `mediaType` or import the generated `RouteManifestResponse`, and Rust code constructing `RouteManifestResponse` directly must populate `has_body` and `media_type`. The route manifest transport/media enums are re-exported from the public prelude for direct construction and matching.
- Generated TypeScript `RouteManifest` entries now include OpenAPI-style route docs metadata: `operationId`, `description`, `tags`, and `deprecated`, alongside the existing `summary`. Documented named routes default `operationId` to the route id, matching OpenAPI output. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; custom route manifest interfaces should add these fields or import the generated `RouteManifestEntry`.
- `RouteManifest.ts` now exports typed route selectors such as `isRouteName()`, `routeManifestEntry()`, `routeEntries()`, `routeRequiresAuth()`, `routePermissions()`, `routeTags()`, `routeResponses()`, `routeRequestSchema()`, `routeRequestTransport()`, `routeRequestMediaType()`, `routeResponseSchemas()`, `routeResponseStatuses()`, `routeResponseMediaTypes()`, `routeResponseBodyFlags()`, `routeResponseByStatus()`, `routeOperationId()`, `routeSummary()`, `routeDescription()`, `routeIsDeprecated()`, `routesRequiringAuth()`, `publicRoutes()`, `clientExportedRoutes()`, `deprecatedRoutes()`, `routesByMethod()`, `routesWithRequestSchema()`, `routesWithRequestTransport()`, `routesWithRequestMediaType()`, `routesWithResponseSchema()`, `routesWithResponseBody()`, `routesWithResponseMediaType()`, `routesWithResponseStatus()`, `routesWithOperationId()`, `routesWithPermission()`, and `routesWithTag()`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; menus, frontend guards, route docs, schema explorers, and route-audit tooling can replace copied `Object.values(RouteManifest)` scans with generated selectors.
- Generated TypeScript `WebSocketChannelIds` now mirrors `RouteIds` by rendering dotted channel ids as a camelCased property tree, while `WebSocketChannelManifest` remains keyed by full channel id strings. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; dotted channel constants should move from bracket access like `WebSocketChannelIds["chat.rooms.updates"]` to property access such as `WebSocketChannelIds.chat.rooms.updates`.
- Generated TypeScript `clientEventToChannel()` now only accepts channels whose backend WebSocket options enable `allow_client_events(true)`, through the generated `WebSocketClientEventChannelName` type. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; any frontend call that sends a client event on a read-only channel should either enable `allow_client_events(true)` in Rust or stop sending that client event.
- WebSocket channels can now register backend-owned client event ids with `WebSocketChannelOptions::client_event(...)` / `client_events(...)`. Registered event ids are enforced at runtime, emitted as `clientEvents` in `WebSocketChannelManifest`, and narrow the generated `WebSocketClientEventName` / `clientEventToChannel()` event argument; channels that only use `allow_client_events(true)` still allow arbitrary event strings for compatibility. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; if constructing `WebSocketChannelDescriptor` directly, populate the new `client_events` field; frontend calls that send unregistered client event ids should register them in Rust or stop sending them.
- WebSocket channels can now document backend-published event ids with `WebSocketChannelOptions::server_event(...)` / `server_events(...)`. These ids are emitted as `serverEvents` in `WebSocketChannelManifest`, narrow `WebSocketServerEventName` / `WebSocketServerFrame`, and are enforced by `WebSocketPublisher` for registered channels whose server-event list is nonempty, including publishes from queued jobs and scheduler tasks booted with the app's WebSocket routes. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; if constructing `WebSocketChannelDescriptor` directly, populate the new `server_events` field; backend publishes to channels with declared server events must use one of those Rust-registered event ids, while channels without declarations remain open for compatibility.
- Generated TypeScript `WebSocketChannelManifest.ts` now exports `WebSocketProtocol`, protocol frame payload/types, `isWebSocketChannelName()`, `isWebSocketProtocolFrame()`, `isWebSocketServerEventName()`, `isWebSocketServerFrame()`, and `parseWebSocketServerFrame()` so frontend clients can validate raw socket JSON against backend-owned protocol, channel, and server-event metadata before dispatching payloads. The parser accepts valid Foundry protocol frames first, then falls back to app server-event metadata so declared app events that reuse channel protocol names are not dropped.
- Built-in broadcast notifications now publish to the canonical WebSocket channel `NOTIFICATION_BROADCAST_CHANNEL` (`"notifications"`) with room set to the notifiable id and event `NOTIFICATION_BROADCAST_EVENT` (`"notification"`), instead of publishing to dynamic channel ids like `notifications:{id}`. **Consumer follow-up:** register `NOTIFICATION_BROADCAST_CHANNEL` in WebSocket routes, include `server_event(NOTIFICATION_BROADCAST_EVENT)` when using server-event allowlists, regenerate frontend types, and update clients to subscribe to channel `"notifications"` with the current user's room id.
- Generated TypeScript `RouteManifest.ts` now exports `RouteManifestEntry` and `RouteManifestResponse` and validates the manifest object against that shape, so frontend guards/navigation/tooling can type against backend-owned route metadata. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; replace hand-written route manifest interfaces with the generated types where possible.
- Generated TypeScript `RouteManifestEntry.method` now uses exported `RouteHttpMethod | null`, and `FoundryHttpMethod` aliases that manifest-owned type instead of duplicating the HTTP method union. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; route tooling that typed manifest methods as arbitrary strings should switch to `RouteHttpMethod`.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint helpers no longer default missing route method metadata to `GET` during `submitForm()` / `submitResponse()`. They now throw unless the route helper has backend method metadata or the submit call passes `options.method`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; named routes registered through generic `route_named(...)` APIs should use typed registrar/scope helpers such as `routes.post(...)` / `routes.get(...)`, add route docs with the method, or pass `method` explicitly when submitting.
- Generated TypeScript `RouteManifest` entries now include `requiresAuth`, matching route options that require authentication through guards, permissions, or dynamic `authorize(...)` callbacks. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; frontend route guards and tooling should read `requiresAuth` instead of inferring auth from `guard`/`permissions`. Rust code constructing `RouteManifestEntry` directly must populate the new `requires_auth` field.
- Generated TypeScript route helpers now export status-keyed `{RouteName}Responses` / `{RouteName}RawResponse` aliases and `FoundryEndpoint.submitResponse()` for clients that need typed access to the HTTP status alongside response data. Existing `submitForm()` behavior is unchanged. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; status-aware screens can switch from `submitForm()` to `submitResponse()` instead of duplicating route response maps by hand.
- `FoundryEndpoint.submitResponse()` now verifies that the HTTP adapter returned a numeric integer `status` before exposing the status-discriminated response type. `submitForm()` still works with data-only adapters. **Consumer follow-up:** custom HTTP adapters used with `submitResponse()` must include the actual response status, for example `{ data, status }`.
- `FoundryEndpoint.submitResponse()` now rejects numeric statuses that are not listed in the generated route manifest, keeping `{RouteName}RawResponse` aligned with backend `response::<T>(status)` metadata. **Consumer follow-up:** document additional route statuses in Rust before relying on them from status-aware frontend code, or use the lower-level HTTP client for intentionally undocumented responses.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint helpers now call `FoundryHttpClient.request` with `FoundryResponseData<{RouteName}Responses>`, the union of every documented response body, instead of only the 2xx success body. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; custom generic HTTP adapters and mocks may now see documented error/no-content payload types when route helpers submit requests.
- Generated TypeScript route helpers for `request::<()>()` now default their `void` request argument to `undefined`, so no-body documented endpoints can be called without passing placeholder data. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; callers can drop explicit `undefined` arguments for affected helpers.
- Generated TypeScript route helpers for nullable request bodies (`request::<Option<T>>()`) now default the helper data argument to `null`, skip client-side validation when the root body is `null`/`undefined`, and still reuse the inner DTO validation rules when an object is provided. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; nullable-body route helpers can now be called without placeholder data, while object payloads may receive the same generated client validation as non-nullable DTO routes.
- Generated TypeScript route helpers for array and string-keyed map request bodies (`request::<Vec<T>>()`, `request::<HashMap<String, T>>()`, and `request::<BTreeMap<String, T>>()`) now reuse `T`'s validation metadata for each item/value instead of emitting an empty client validation schema. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; bulk endpoint helpers may now show client-side validation errors before submit where the backend already rejected invalid item DTOs.
- Generated TypeScript route helpers for nested request containers such as `request::<HashMap<String, Vec<T>>>()` now walk every container layer and reuse `T`'s validation metadata for the innermost DTO. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; nested bulk endpoint helpers may now report indexed client-side validation errors before submit.
- Generated TypeScript route helpers for paths with params now require typed path params when creating the endpoint instance and reuse them for `submitForm()` / `submitResponse()` unless a submit call overrides `params`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; calls to parameterized route helpers should move route params into the factory call, e.g. `AdminUsersShow(api, { id })` or `AdminUsersUpdate(api, { id }, data)`.
- Generated TypeScript route helper `patchData()` is now typed and guarded for object-like request bodies only instead of silently reshaping arrays, files, scalars, or no-body requests into accidental objects. `setData()` remains available for replacing any request body. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; frontend code that patched array/file/scalar helpers should switch to `setData()`.
- Rust validation and generated TypeScript endpoint validation now resolve custom messages and display attributes for `each(...)` item errors through the base field name (for example `tags[0]` uses the `tags` attribute and `messages(tags(...))` overrides), with generated client messages interpolating `{{attribute}}` and rule parameters like Rust. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types to pick up the client-side message parity fix; apps with base-field custom messages for collection fields may see those messages applied to item errors instead of generic fallbacks.
- Generated OpenAPI operations now include Foundry auth metadata from route options under `x-foundry-auth` (`required`, `guard`, and `permissions`) instead of leaving generated API docs blind to guarded routes. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate OpenAPI clients/docs; custom tooling can read `x-foundry-auth` instead of duplicating route manifest auth metadata.
- Generated OpenAPI operations for named routes now default `operationId` to the route id, and routes can override it with `RouteDoc::operation_id(...)` / `HttpRouteOptions::operation_id(...)`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate OpenAPI clients; generated method names may stabilize around route ids or explicit overrides instead of tool-inferred path names.
- Generated OpenAPI route paths now reject blank, padded, or relative path strings before generation, normalize Axum catch-all `{*path}` and legacy `:id` segments to standard OpenAPI `{path}` / `{id}` templates, and emit required `in: path` parameter entries. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate OpenAPI clients; direct route docs should use backend-style absolute paths such as `/users/{id}`, and catch-all / legacy-param routes may appear under normalized path templates with typed path parameters.
- Derived OpenAPI schemas now expose more `#[validate(...)]` rules as JSON Schema: `regex(...)`, `not_regex(...)`, `starts_with(...)`, `doesnt_start_with(...)`, `ends_with(...)`, `doesnt_end_with(...)`, `contains(...)`, `alpha`, `alpha_num`, `alpha_numeric`, `alpha_dash`, `ulid`, `hex_color`, `mac_address`, `decimal(...)`, `ascii`, `digits`, `min_digits(...)`, `max_digits(...)`, `digits_between(...)`, date/time formats, `ipv4`/`ipv6`, `between(...)`, `multiple_of(...)`, `in_list(...)`, `not_in(...)`, and `app_enum(...)` where the field schema does not already expose enum values. Supported `each(...)` validation constraints also apply to array item schemas, and validation-only `message = "..."` overrides are ignored while preserving the underlying constraint. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate OpenAPI clients/docs; generated validators may become stricter where DTOs use these rules, and custom `regex(...)` patterns should stay compatible with any OpenAPI client generator that consumes the schema `pattern`.
- OpenAPI request bodies whose schema contains `UploadedFile` now use `multipart/form-data` instead of `application/json`, and generated TypeScript endpoint helpers now serialize direct `File` / `File[]` request aliases into `FormData` under a stable `file` field by default. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate OpenAPI clients; file upload endpoints may switch generated client methods to multipart. If a direct-file endpoint expects a different root field name, pass `formDataField` when submitting.
- Route helper response aliases generated for TypeScript now preserve string-keyed map response shapes from `BTreeMap<String, T>` and `HashMap<String, T>` route docs as `Record<string, T>` instead of falling back to `unknown`.
- Derived OpenAPI schemas now treat `serde_json::Value` fields as unconstrained JSON instead of incorrectly narrowing them to objects.
- Derived OpenAPI schemas now follow serde field and unit-enum variant wire names from `rename` / `rename_all`, keeping OpenAPI property names aligned with JSON payloads and generated TypeScript.
- Derived OpenAPI schemas now expand `#[serde(flatten)]` fields into parent-level properties, including nested required fields for non-optional flattened DTOs, so documented payloads match serde's flattened JSON shape.
- Derived OpenAPI schemas and generated route helper aliases now cover the common Rust integer primitive widths (`u8`, `u16`, `usize`, `isize`, etc.) instead of falling back to unsupported trait bounds or `unknown`.
- `()` now implements `ApiSchema`, derived OpenAPI schemas render unit fields as JSON `null`, OpenAPI responses for `()`/204/205/304 omit JSON content, and generated TypeScript route helpers render unit/no-content route responses as `void`, making `response::<()>(204)` usable for typed no-content endpoints. **Consumer follow-up:** OpenAPI-generated clients that previously expected JSON content on no-content statuses should treat those responses as bodyless.
- OpenAPI route schemas now inline nullable and generic wrapper request/response shapes (`Option<T>`, `Vec<T>`, and string-keyed maps) instead of storing them under colliding component names such as `String`, `Array`, or `Map`. This prevents one route's `Option<String>` or `Vec<User>` docs from overwriting another route's non-null `String` or differently typed collection component. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate OpenAPI clients; affected wrapper/nullable route schemas may appear inline instead of as shared `$ref` components.
- Generated TypeScript route helpers now preserve documented request container shapes (`Vec<T>`, string-keyed maps) and nullable route schemas from `Option<T>`, instead of collapsing collection requests to `unknown` or omitting `null` from response aliases. `RouteManifestEntry::request` now owns the rendered schema name as `Option<String>` so request wrappers can be represented the same way response wrappers are. **Consumer follow-up:** frontend code importing affected route helper aliases may now need explicit array/map payloads and null checks where route docs use `Vec<_>`, `HashMap<String, _>`, `BTreeMap<String, _>`, or `Option<_>`; Rust code constructing or matching `RouteManifestEntry` directly should use `Some("Schema".to_string())` or `request.as_deref()`.
- Generated TypeScript route helpers now render Foundry scalar route schemas (`DateTime`, `LocalDateTime`, `Date`, `Time`, `Numeric`, `ModelId`, semantic IDs, `Uuid`) as `string` and `UploadedFile` as browser `File` instead of `unknown`. `uuid::Uuid` also implements `ApiSchema` directly for route docs. **Consumer follow-up:** frontend code that treated these route helper request/response aliases as `unknown` should remove casts and handle them as strings or `File` values.
- Generated TypeScript route helpers now render `serde_json::Value` route schemas through the generated recursive `JsonValue` union instead of object-only or broad `unknown` aliases, matching scalar/array/object/null JSON payloads while keeping JSON property access explicit. String-keyed maps of JSON values render as `Record<string, JsonValue>`. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; frontend code that assumed JSON route aliases were always objects should narrow the value before property access.
- Derived OpenAPI schemas now treat non-`required` `#[serde(default)]` fields as optional and require matching TypeScript optional metadata for non-`Option` defaults, preventing backend-accepted omissions from becoming frontend type errors.
- Generated TypeScript now exports `DatatableRequest` defaulted request fields (`page`, `per_page`, `sort`, `filters`, `search`) as optional, matching the backend defaults accepted by serde. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; strict request builders no longer need to send `search: null` when no search term is active.
- `DatatableJsonResponse.columns` now includes backend-owned `exportable` and nullable `relation` metadata from `DatatableColumn`, and the generated TypeScript/OpenAPI `DatatableColumnMeta` contract reflects those fields. **Consumer follow-up:** regenerate frontend types; table UIs and export controls can stop duplicating exportability/relation flags, while strict response mocks should add `exportable` and `relation`.
- Generated TypeScript registration now requires `#[ts(optional)]` on fields using `#[serde(skip_serializing_if = "...")]`, and derived OpenAPI schemas leave those sparse fields out of `required`, preventing response fields that serde can omit from being documented or exported as always-present frontend properties.
- `#[derive(Validate)]` now validates typed `AppEnum` fields, `Option<AppEnum>` fields, and `Vec<AppEnum>` `each(app_enum(...))` rules through `FoundryAppEnum::key()` instead of requiring consumer enums to implement `Display`/`Default`.
- Generated TypeScript validation metadata now includes the same derived `nullable` rule that Rust applies to non-`required` `Option<T>` fields, so optional DTO fields do not fail client-side validation while passing server-side validation.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint validation now rejects empty, whitespace-only, and JavaScript-only numeric literal input before `Number(...)` coercion, validates `integer` as a Rust `i64` shape (including range checks), and lets non-`required` `alpha`/`alpha_numeric`/`digits` fields accept empty strings, matching the Rust validator's semantics.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint `email` validation now mirrors the Rust `validator` crate more closely, including single-label domains, IP-literal domains, local/domain length limits, and rejection of invalid domain labels such as underscores.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint validation now prevalidates file metadata rules that are safe to check in the browser (`max_file_size` and `allowed_extensions`) while keeping content-sniffing file rules (`image`, `allowed_mimes`, image dimensions) marked as server-only metadata.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint `uuid` validation now accepts UUIDv7 and the common Rust parser forms (`simple`, hyphenated, braced, and `urn:uuid:`) instead of rejecting anything outside UUID versions 1-5.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint `ip`, `ipv4`, and `ipv6` validation now mirrors Rust parser semantics more closely: invalid IPv6 shapes such as `::::` fail client-side, leading-zero IPv4 octets are rejected, and IPv4-mapped IPv6 addresses such as `::ffff:192.0.2.128` are accepted.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint `date`, `time`, `datetime`, `local_datetime`, and temporal comparison validation now uses strict Rust-shaped parsing instead of broad browser `Date.parse` coercion. Client-side validation now rejects normalized calendar overflows such as `2026-02-30`, requires seconds for `time`, preserves leap-second acceptance, and rejects date-only `datetime` values.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint `timezone` validation now trims input and accepts case-insensitive `UTC`, matching the Rust validator.
- Generated TypeScript endpoint `regex` validation now constructs client-side patterns with the Unicode flag, matching Rust regex behavior for Unicode character classes such as `\p{L}` while Rust-only patterns are represented as server-only validation metadata.
- A worker whose job-lease heartbeat fails (lease expired, claimed elsewhere, or backend unreachable past the lease TTL) now cancels the running job instead of letting it race the redelivered copy on another worker. Transient renewal errors are retried while the last successful renewal still covers the lease TTL.
- Plugins that booted successfully are now shut down (in reverse order) when a later plugin's `boot()` fails, so resources acquired during partial bootstrap no longer leak.
- The in-memory scheduler leadership backend no longer renews an already-expired lease; like the Redis backend, the previous holder must win a fresh election, preventing split-brain in single-process and test setups.
- The WebSocket pub/sub task now resubscribes with exponential backoff when its backend subscription ends or fails, instead of going permanently silent while publishes keep succeeding; dropping the server also aborts the task instead of leaking it.
- Scheduler leadership state uses acquire/release atomic ordering, and dropping the scheduler or a schedule overlap-lock guard outside a Tokio runtime now logs a warning instead of silently leaving the lock to lapse via TTL.
- Image dimension validation streams the upload from disk on the blocking thread pool instead of reading the entire file into memory on the async runtime.

### Added

- TypeScript route endpoint helpers: `types:export` now emits a headless `FoundryEndpoint` base runtime plus per-route helper files with path/method constants, request/response aliases, typed `validateForm()`/`submitForm()`, busy/error state, and validation metadata from `#[derive(Validate)]`. Generated DTO files now include a Foundry do-not-edit header, and validated DTO fields include validation-rule comments. Routes can opt out with `without_client_export()` or `client_export(false)`.
- Datatable relation filters: model datatables can opt in to typed relation-backed filters with `Datatable::relation_filters()`, `DatatableRelationFilter`, and `DatatableRelationColumn`.
- Datatable relation filter coverage for belongs-to, has-many, many-to-many, legacy hyphen aliases, and `LikeAny` search across declared relation columns.
- Consumer-facing datatable request examples for direct filters, relation filters, legacy query params, and multi-column relation search.
- Release infrastructure: GitHub Actions CI, release-readiness workflow, release checklist, and local package dry-run verification.
- Consumer documentation: root README, contributing guide, and a first-class plugin example.
- WebSocket observability dashboard endpoints: `GET /_foundry/ws/channels`, `GET /_foundry/ws/presence/:channel`, `GET /_foundry/ws/history/:channel`, and `GET /_foundry/ws/stats`. History payloads are redacted by default; set `observability.websocket.include_payloads = true` to include them.
- Per-channel WebSocket Prometheus series on `/_foundry/metrics` (`foundry_websocket_subscriptions_total{channel=...}`, `foundry_websocket_active_subscriptions{channel=...}`, `foundry_websocket_channel_messages_total{channel=...,direction=...}`).
- HTTP request latency histograms on `/_foundry/runtime` and `/_foundry/metrics` via `foundry_http_request_duration_ms_bucket`, `_sum`, and `_count`, which can be used to compute p50/p95/p99 in Prometheus-compatible backends.
- `AppContext::websocket_channels()` accessor returning the registered channel registry.
- `WebSocketChannelDescriptor` and `WebSocketChannelRegistry` public types exposing registered WebSocket channels.
- Configurable TTL on WebSocket replay history (`websocket.history_ttl_seconds`, default 7 days). Every publish refreshes the TTL on `ws:history:<channel>`, so active channels never expire; channels idle past the window are auto-reaped by Redis. Set to `0` to disable.
- WebSocket hardening config: `websocket.outbound_buffer_size`, `websocket.allowed_origins`, and `websocket.history_buffer_size`.
- WebSocket protocol/lifecycle acceptance coverage for raw JSON actions, subscription enforcement, room routing, client events, ack success/error, socket-close cleanup, and force-disconnect cleanup.
- `doctor --strict` for production readiness gates; warnings now fail the command in strict mode and text output ends with a readiness verdict.
- `make:model`, `make:job`, and `make:command` now accept `--path <DIR>` and are registered even when a project has not published database config yet.
- Public API contract and recipe documentation covering production readiness, authenticated CRUD, queued email, uploads, datatables, and plugin extension.
- Public API acceptance coverage for the blessed consumer import surface.

### Changed

- Config env overrides now support an explicit `FOUNDRY__` namespace (e.g. `FOUNDRY__SERVER__PORT`), which is stripped before applying and wins over the unprefixed form. Unprefixed `__`-delimited variables keep working; the prefix avoids collisions with ambient process variables.
- `make:command` now scaffolds commands with the prelude-exported `Command`, avoiding a direct `clap` dependency in newly generated app code. Existing generated commands can keep `clap` in `Cargo.toml` or switch `clap::Command::new(...)` to `Command::new(...)` when importing `foundry::prelude::*`.
- `TemplateRenderer` gained `render_async`, which renders on Tokio's blocking thread pool; `EmailMessage::template(...)` uses it internally.
- `Job::max_retries` and `jobs.max_retries` are now documented as the maximum number of *total attempts* (like Laravel's `tries`): `1` dead-letters on the first failure with no retry.
- `EventManager::dispatch` is now documented as sequential with stop-on-first-error semantics, mirroring Laravel's synchronous listeners.
- Database scaffold command helpers moved out of the migration lifecycle module into a dedicated scaffold module.
- Datatable blueprint/status documentation now reflects implemented JSON, filter, sort, download, export, registry, legacy query-param, and relation-filter acceptance coverage.
- Consumer starter documentation now recommends the split bootstrap layout proven by the blueprint app fixture.
- The README architecture diagram was replaced with an ASCII-safe AppBuilder/AppContext/kernel flow.
- `foundry-build` migration filename tests now assert the current parser diagnostics for invalid timestamps and malformed `YYYYMMDDHHMM_slug.rs` filenames.
- Crate metadata is now publish-ready for the `0.1.x` line.
- Verification contract now explicitly includes both fixture families and packaging checks.
- `MaxBodySize` now also updates Axum's default extractor body limit, so JSON/Form/String extractors honor the configured Foundry limit instead of staying capped at Axum's 2 MiB default.
- Framework model post-write events (`ModelCreatedEvent`, `ModelUpdatedEvent`, and `ModelDeletedEvent`) now dispatch after the active transaction commits, making event listeners safe for dependent writes and queued onboarding jobs that need the committed row to be visible.
- `WebSocketRuntimeSnapshot` now includes a `channels: Vec<WebSocketChannelSnapshot>` field in addition to the existing global counters.
